Divine Transcendence
beginner
4 min
The Rational Possibility of Seeing Allah
The poet commands certainty of seeing Allah, citing rational possibility and revealed proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that seeing Allah in Paradise is rationally possible and confirmed by revelation, and why this refutes those who deny the beatific vision.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah is possible by reason, actual by revelation.

The poem begins with a strong command: be certain of seeing Allah in Paradise without end. This certainty rests on two foundations: rational possibility and revealed proof. Before we read the source, note that this doctrine defends the beatific vision against those who claim it is rationally impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on seeing Allah
Read the Arabic lines from 'wa-jzim akhī' to 'dalīl al-naql' along with the translation. Notice the poet's assertive tone.
The phrase 'bi-lā tanāhī' emphasizes that the vision is eternal.
2
Understand the rational judgment
The poet says the occurrence (al-wuqūʿ) is 'jāʾiz bi al-ʿaql' – possible by reason. This means the mind does not see it as necessary or impossible. Identify why this matters in kalam: without rational possibility, revelation cannot affirm it.
Contrast with necessary (wājib) and impossible (mustaḥīl).
3
Connect reason and revelation
The passage then says 'wa qad atā fīhi dalīl al-naql' – and textual evidence has come concerning it. So actual occurrence is known from revelation. See how the poem combines both sources.
This refutes those who say reason alone suffices or that revelation contradicts reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاجْزِمْ أَخِي بِرُؤْيَةِ الإِلَهِ فِي جَنَّةِ الخُلْدِ بِلاَ تَنَاهِي إِذِ الوُقُوعُ جَائِزٌ بِالعَقْلِ وَقَدْ أَتَى فِيْهِ دَلِيلُ النَّقْلِ وَصِفْ جَمِيْعَ الرُّسُلِ بِالأَمَانَةِ وَالصِّدْقِ وَالتَّبْلِيغِ وَالفَطَانَةِ وَيَسْتَحِيْلُ ضِدُّهَا عَلَيْهِمُ وَجَائِزٌ كَالأَكْلِ فِي حَقِّهِمُ إِرْسَالُهُمْ تَفَضُّلٌ وَرَحْمَةٌ لِلْعَالَمِيْنَ جَلَّ مُوْلِي النِّعْمَةِ
And be certain, my brother, of seeing Allah in the Garden of Eternity without end, for the occurrence is possible by reason, and textual evidence has come concerning it. And describe all messengers with trustworthiness, truthfulness, delivery, and intelligence. And their opposite is impossible for them, and what is possible (like eating) is possible in their case. Their sending is a favor and mercy to the worlds, exalted is the Lord of grace.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct topics. First, the poet commands the reader to be certain (ijzim) of seeing Allah (ruʾyat Allāh) in Paradise without end. This is because the occurrence (wuqūʿ) is rationally possible (jāʾiz bi al-ʿaql) and has been confirmed by revealed proof (dalīl al-naql). This refutes those who deny the beatific vision. Second, he lists the necessary attributes of prophets: trustworthiness (amāna), truthfulness (ṣidq), delivery of the message (tablīgh), and intelligence (faṭāna). Their opposites are impossible (mustaḥīl) for them. However, mundane acts like eating are possible (jāʾiz) for them, affirming their humanity. Finally, the sending of prophets is a favor (tafaḍḍul) and mercy (raḥma) from God.

Key Terms
رؤية الله
جائز بالعقل
دليل النقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think seeing Allah is rationally impossible; thus revelation cannot override reason.
Correction: The poem clarifies that it is only rationally possible (not impossible), so revelation can affirm it.

Checkpoint
According to the poem, the permissibility of seeing Allah is established by what?
A) Rational impossibility.
B) Textual evidence only.
C) Rational possibility and textual evidence.
D) Consensus of scholars.

Key Takeaway
Seeing Allah in Paradise is rationally possible and revealed as true, affirming both reason and revelation in theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim certainty of seeing Allah in Paradise. But does that certainty move you to obey Him even when no one is watching? Take a moment to identify one hidden sin you tolerate. What would change if you saw His face right now?
?
Your belief in the beatific vision is built on both reason and revelation. Which is stronger in your heart today: intellectual acceptance or existential longing? Be honest—when was the last time you wept out of love for the meeting with your Lord?
?
If you truly knew you will see Allah without end, would you still love this world so fiercely? What worldly attachment would you struggle to release? Ask Allah tonight to make your certainty real enough to loosen that grip.

The Attributes of Prophets and Their Sending
The poet enumerates prophetic attributes and the nature of prophethood as favor and mercy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four necessary attributes of prophets, their opposites which are impossible, the permissible human acts, and that prophethood is a divine favor and mercy.

Core Idea
Prophets must be truthful, trustworthy, intelligent, and deliver the message; they remain human.

After discussing divine vision, the poem turns to prophethood. It lists the essential qualities every messenger must possess, clarifies what cannot be in them, and acknowledges their humanity. Finally, it explains why Allah sends prophets. This passage grounds the Islamic understanding of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the full prophetic section
Read the Arabic from 'wa-sif jamīʿa' to the end, and the corresponding translation. Notice the three categories: necessary (amāna, ṣidq, tablīgh, faṭāna), impossible (their opposites), and possible (like eating).
The list is concise; memorize these four attributes.
2
Understand the threefold classification
In kalam, prophets (like Allah) are described in terms of necessary, impossible, and possible attributes. Identify each in the passage: necessary virtues, impossible vices, and permissible human acts.
This classification mirrors the one used for Allah but applied to prophets.
3
Reflect on the reason for sending prophets
The final line states that sending prophets is tafaddul (favor) and raḥma (mercy) from Allah to the worlds. Ask: Why is it a favor? What would be missing without prophets?
This emphasizes Allah's benevolence and the need for guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاجْزِمْ أَخِي بِرُؤْيَةِ الإِلَهِ فِي جَنَّةِ الخُلْدِ بِلاَ تَنَاهِي إِذِ الوُقُوعُ جَائِزٌ بِالعَقْلِ وَقَدْ أَتَى فِيْهِ دَلِيلُ النَّقْلِ وَصِفْ جَمِيْعَ الرُّسُلِ بِالأَمَانَةِ وَالصِّدْقِ وَالتَّبْلِيغِ وَالفَطَانَةِ وَيَسْتَحِيْلُ ضِدُّهَا عَلَيْهِمُ وَجَائِزٌ كَالأَكْلِ فِي حَقِّهِمُ إِرْسَالُهُمْ تَفَضُّلٌ وَرَحْمَةٌ لِلْعَالَمِيْنَ جَلَّ مُوْلِي النِّعْمَةِ
And be certain, my brother, of seeing Allah in the Garden of Eternity without end, for the occurrence is possible by reason, and textual evidence has come concerning it. And describe all messengers with trustworthiness, truthfulness, delivery, and intelligence. And their opposite is impossible for them, and what is possible (like eating) is possible in their case. Their sending is a favor and mercy to the worlds, exalted is the Lord of grace.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct topics. First, the poet commands the reader to be certain (ijzim) of seeing Allah (ruʾyat Allāh) in Paradise without end. This is because the occurrence (wuqūʿ) is rationally possible (jāʾiz bi al-ʿaql) and has been confirmed by revealed proof (dalīl al-naql). This refutes those who deny the beatific vision. Second, he lists the necessary attributes of prophets: trustworthiness (amāna), truthfulness (ṣidq), delivery of the message (tablīgh), and intelligence (faṭāna). Their opposites are impossible (mustaḥīl) for them. However, mundane acts like eating are possible (jāʾiz) for them, affirming their humanity. Finally, the sending of prophets is a favor (tafaḍḍul) and mercy (raḥma) from God.

Key Terms
أمانة
صدق
تبليغ
فطنة
تفضل
رحمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets are infallible only in delivering revelation but may sin in other matters; or they are not fully human.
Correction: Prophets are protected from all sins and from qualities opposite to their necessary attributes, yet they experience human needs like eating.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the necessary attributes of prophets mentioned in the poem?
A) Trustworthiness (amāna)
B) Truthfulness (ṣidq)
C) Infallibility from all sins (ʿiṣma)
D) Intelligence (faṭāna)

Key Takeaway
Prophets must have four essential virtues, are free from their opposites, share human traits, and are sent as a mercy from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If prophets are sent as mercy for the worlds, do you truly treat the teachings of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as a mercy in your daily life? What is one command of his you have been negligent in that you will act upon today?
?
You believe the Prophet is truthful and trustworthy—but are you truthful and trustworthy in your speech and promises? Think of a recent lie or broken promise; what step will you take to rectify it before tomorrow?
?
Prophets ate and drank like you, yet they lived lives of complete submission. What is one area of your life where you have excused yourself by saying 'I'm only human'? Starting now, what prophet-like habit will you adopt this week despite your human weakness?

Divine Transcendence

Knowledge of Allah is About His Attributes
al-Sawi defines knowledge of Allah as knowing His attributes, not His essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that knowledge of Allah in Islam is about His attributes (what is necessary, impossible, and permissible) and not about comprehending His essence, and why that is impossible.

Core Idea
Knowing Allah means knowing what He must be, cannot be, and may be, not what He is in Himself.

This lesson clarifies the primary goal of Islamic theology. The author, al-Sawi, explains that when we speak of knowing Allah, we are not trying to grasp His infinite essence. Instead, we are to know the categories of what is necessary, impossible, and possible for Him. This distinction shapes all subsequent theological arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage includes a poem, so read it as a complete unit.
2
Identify the three categories
Find the three Arabic terms for necessary, impossible, and permissible (ما يجب, ما يستحيل, ما يجوز). Notice how the author defines knowledge of Allah through these three.
These three categories are the foundation of all kalam discussions about Allah.
3
Understand the limitation
The author stresses that knowing the essence of Allah is not required and is impossible for any creature, both rationally and legally. Reflect on why this is a key point.
Even the highest spiritual rank cannot attain this.
4
Reflect on the poem
Read the poem by al-Sharif al-Maqdisi. It reinforces the humility of the intellect before Allah's greatness. Consider how the poem supports the author's argument.
The poem is a beautiful expression of tanzih (transcendence).
5
Connect to the learning objective
Now that you have engaged with the passage, explain in your own words what knowledge of Allah means according to this text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما كانت معرفة الله تعالى عبارة عن معرفة ما يجب في تعالى وما يستحيل وما يجوز، لا معرفة حقيقة الذات العليَّة؛ لأنَّها ليست من الواجبات فضلاً عن كونها من أوَّلها، بل لا تعرف لأحد ولو ارتفعت درجته، وإن أمكنت معرفتها عقلاً كذا قيل، والأصح أنَّها لا تجوز عقلاً كما لا تجوز شرعاً، كما في شرح الكبرى عن الإمام الغزالي، فإنَّ الحادث يقصر بالطبع عن عظيم هذا المقام، قال الشَّريف المقدسي في مفاتيح الكنوز : [ من البسيط] ظننت جهلاً بأنَّ الله تدركه ثواقبُ الفِكْر أو تدريه إيقانا أو العقول أحاطته بديهتها أو هل أقامت به لولاه برهانا الله أعظم قدراً أن يُحيط به عِلم وعقل ورأي جل سلطانا هذا اعتقادي فإن قصرتُ في عملي فأسأل الله توفيقاً وغفرانا
And since knowledge of Allah the Exalted is an expression of knowing what is necessary for the Exalted, what is impossible for Him, and what is permissible for Him, not knowing the reality of the Supreme Essence; because it is not among the obligations, let alone being the first of them. Rather, it is not known to anyone even if his rank is elevated, and even if its knowledge were possible by reason, as has been said, the soundest view is that it is not permissible by reason just as it is not permissible by law, as in Sharh al-Kubra from Imam al-Ghazali, for the contingent is naturally incapable of [comprehending] the greatness of this station. Al-Sharif al-Maqdisi said in Mafatih al-Kunuz: [al-Basit] I ignorantly thought that Allah can be attained by piercing intellects or known with certainty, or that minds encompass Him in their intuition, or that proofs about Him are established without Him. Allah is too great to be encompassed by knowledge, intellect, or opinion; majestic is His authority. This is my belief, and if I fall short in my deeds, I ask Allah for success and forgiveness.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage defines what 'knowledge of Allah' actually means: it is knowledge of what is necessary (wajib), impossible (mustahil), and permissible (ja'iz) for Him — not knowledge of His essence (dhat). The author argues that even knowing the essence is not obligatory, nor is it even possible for anyone, regardless of spiritual rank. Although some claimed it might be rationally possible, the preferred view (as stated by al-Ghazali in Sharh al-Kubra) is that it is neither rationally nor legally possible because the contingent creature is inherently incapable of grasping the Creator's majesty. This is reinforced by a poem from al-Sharif al-Maqdisi, which dismisses any claim to encompass Allah's reality through intellect or proof, concluding with a plea for divine forgiveness.

Key Terms
معرفة الله
ما يجب
ما يستحيل
ما يجوز
حقيقة الذات
الحادث
الغزالي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The goal of Islamic theology is to comprehend Allah's essence.
Correction: Rather, theology aims to know His necessary, impossible, and permissible attributes, as the essence is beyond comprehension.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does knowledge of Allah consist of?
A) Knowing His essence
B) Knowing what is necessary, impossible, and permissible for Him
C) Knowing His names only
D) Knowing His actions only

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of Allah is understanding His necessary, impossible, and permissible attributes, not comprehending His essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself thinking you 'understand' Allah or have figured Him out? What does this lesson reveal about that assumption, and how should it change your approach to knowing Him?
?
The poem confesses 'I ignorantly thought that Allah can be attained by piercing intellects.' In what areas of your life do you still rely on your intellect to 'grasp' Allah, rather than humbly accepting His transcendence?
?
If true knowledge of Allah is limited to His attributes, not His essence, how should that affect the way you speak about Him in your daily conversations and even in your worship?

Divine Blessings and the Obligation of Obedience
Al-Sawi presents a reflection on divine blessings as evidence for God's mercy and the duty of obedience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how reflecting on God's blessings in creation leads to the recognition of His mercy and the duty of obedience.

Core Idea
Reflecting on blessings reveals God's mercy and demands our obedience.

This passage from al-Sawi's commentary invites us to contemplate the intricate wisdom in our own bodies and the cosmos. It shows that every moment of existence is filled with divine blessings, which call for gratitude and obedience. The text moves from the digestion process to breath, intellect, and finally the heavens and earth, all as signs of the Beneficent Bestower.

Guided Path
1
Read the Reflection
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Let the description of bodily processes and the supplication resonate.
Notice the transition from internal to external signs.
2
Identify the Moral Conclusion
Find the rhetorical question 'Should this God be disobeyed?' and understand why it follows the enumeration of blessings.
This is the core argument: blessings imply gratitude and obedience.
3
Examine the Structure
Trace the progression: bodily functions, intellect, cosmic signs. Each leads to amazement and recognition of the Bestower.
The structure builds from personal to universal signs.
4
Reflect on the Supplication
The passage ends with a prayer. Consider how the reflection naturally leads to a response of humble request.
The supplication is a model of gratitude and dependence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفة الوجود فإذا نزل الطعام والشراب في المعدة صرفه إلى ما يشاء، فبعضُه يتربى به اللحم، وبعضُه يتربَّى به العظم، وبعضه يتربى به الشحم، وبعضُه يتربّى به الدَّم مع كمال اللَّذَّة حال الأكل وبعده، ثمَّ ما فضل عن ذلك وكان فيه الإيذاء للبدن على تقدير إبقائه في البطن أخرجه من مخرجيك، وانظر إلى هذين المخرجين وبديع حكمتهما وإلى إقدارك على إمساكهما عند تهيؤ الفضلة للخروج .وبالجملة فلم يزل سبحانه بك رؤوفاً رحيماً ودوداً كريماً في كلِّ لحظة وأنت غافل عن نفسك.وانظر إلى خروج النَّفَس ودخوله الذي به قوام الرُّوح حالة اليقظة والنَّوم والصحة والمرض . ومن أكبر عبرة: العقلُ الذي به التَّمييز والتَّدبير وإدراك العلوم والمعارف وما يضرُّ وما ينفع وَإِن تَعُدُّوا نِعْمَتَ اللَّهِ لَا تُحْصُوهَا ) فَتَبَارَكَ اللهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخَلِقِينَ) فـيـا ليت شعري أهذا ينبغي أن يعصى فيما أمر ونهى؟!! ثمَّ إذا نظرت إلى السَّماء وكواكبها والسَّحاب وتسخيرها، والرِّيَاح وتصريفها، وإلى الأرض ،وأنهارها ، وإلى الأشجار وأثمارها ؛ لأفضى بك إلى العجب العجاب وعلمتَ أن المحسن الوهّاب. اللَّهُمَّ ؛ وَفّقنا لما فيه رضاك، واقطعنا عن كلِّ شيء سواك، واملأ قلوبنا من حبّك وحب رسلك، وأذقنا لَذَّة الوصل من فيض فضلك، وخذ بأيدينا إن زللنا وسامحنا إن أخطأنا إنك أنت الجواد الكريم الرؤوف الرحيم .قوله : (أخرجه من مخرجيك) : أي ومن حكمته تعالى أن جعلهما لأسفل ؛ لئلا يتأذَى برؤيتهما الغير، فأظهر منك المحاسن وأخفى القبائح. قوله : (إلى خروج النَّفَس) : بفتحتين . قوله : ( وَإِن تَعُدُّوا نِعْمَتَ اللَّهِ لَا تُحْصُوهَا ) مفرد مضاف؛ أي: نعمه . قوله : ( فَتَبَارَكَ اللهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخَلِقِينَ ) : اسم التفضيل ليس على بابه، أو باعتبار الصورة الظاهرية. قوله: (أهذا ينبغي أن يعصى) أي من صدرت منه هذه الأفعال العظيمة، التي هي قائمة بك وأنت جاهل بها ولا تدريها، فالواجب عليك أيُّها الشَّخص امتثال أوامره واجتناب نواهيه ولا تجترئ على معرفة ذات خالقك ؛ فإنَّك جاهل بنفسك فكيف بربك. قوله : (ثم إذا نظرت إلى السَّماء . . . إلخ) : المراد العالم العلوي . وقوله : (وإلى الأرض ... إلخ) : المراد : العالم السفلي . قوله : لأفضى بك) : أي : لأداك ووصلك .
The attribute of existence. When food and drink descend into the stomach, He directs it as He wills: some of it nourishes the flesh, some of it nourishes the bone, some of it nourishes the fat, and some of it nourishes the blood, with complete pleasure during and after eating. Then what remains beyond that and would cause harm to the body if left in the belly, He expels from your two exits. And consider these two exits and the wonderful wisdom in them, and His enabling you to hold them back when the waste is ready to exit. In summary, He—glorified and exalted—has not ceased being kind, merciful, affectionate, generous to you at every moment, while you are heedless of yourself. And consider the exhalation and inhalation of breath, by which the spirit is sustained, in wakefulness, sleep, health, and sickness. Among the greatest signs is the intellect, by which discrimination, management, and the perception of sciences and knowledge, and what harms and benefits, [are achieved]. "And if you should count the favors of Allah, you could not enumerate them" [Ibrahim 34], "So blessed is Allah, the best of creators" [Al-Mu'minun 14]. O, I wish I knew—should this [God] be disobeyed in what He commands and forbids?! Then, when you look at the sky and its stars, the clouds and their subjugation, the winds and their disposition, and at the earth and its rivers, and at the trees and their fruits, it will lead you to wondrous amazement and you will know that the Benefactor is the Bestower. O Allah! Grant us success in that which pleases You, cut us off from everything other than You, fill our hearts with love for You and love for Your messengers, let us taste the sweetness of union from the abundance of Your grace, take hold of our hands if we slip, and pardon us if we err. Indeed, You are the Generous, the Kind, the Compassionate, the Merciful. His saying: "He expels from your two exits" means: and from His wisdom—exalted is He—that He made them downward so that others are not harmed by seeing them; He manifested your good features and concealed the ugly ones. His saying: "to the exhalation of the breath" means with two fathas. His saying: "And if you should count the favors of Allah, you could not enumerate them" is a singular noun in construct state, i.e., His favors. His saying: "So blessed is Allah, the best of creators" means: the superlative form is not used in its literal sense, or it is in consideration of the outward form. His saying: "Should this be disobeyed" means: from Him who performed these great acts, which are subsisting through you while you are ignorant of them and unaware of them, so the duty upon you, O person, is to obey His commands and avoid His prohibitions, and do not dare to seek knowledge of the essence of your Creator, for you are ignorant of yourself, so how [can you know] your Lord? His saying: "Then when you look at the sky... etc." means: the upper world. And his saying: "and at the earth... etc." means: the lower world. His saying: "it will lead you" means: it will bring and convey you.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a reflective commentary on the divine attribute of existence (صفة الوجود), likely from the original sharh, with marginal glosses from al-Sawi. It begins by describing the wisdom in the process of digestion: food is distributed to different parts of the body, and waste is expelled from two exits placed downward for modesty. The point is to show God's ongoing kindness and mercy, even as humans remain heedless. Then it considers the breath essential for life and the intellect as a great sign for distinguishing benefit and harm. Two Quranic verses are cited to emphasize the impossibility of enumerating God's favors and to declare Him the best of creators. The rhetorical question 'should this God be disobeyed?' drives home the moral obligation of obedience. The passage then extends the reflection to the cosmos—sky, stars, clouds, winds, earth, rivers, trees, fruits—as signs that lead to amazement and recognition of God as the Beneficent Bestower. The lesson concludes with a supplication for divine guidance, love, and forgiveness. The marginal notes (قوله) explain specific phrases: the placement of the excretory organs as a divine wisdom, the vocalization of 'النَّفَس', the grammatical interpretation of 'نِعْمَتَ' as a singular noun in construct state meaning all favors, the nuance of the superlative in 'أحسن الخالقين' (either not literal or referring outward form), the moral implication of the rhetorical question (obedience required from one who cannot even know his own self, let alone God's essence), and the cosmological reference to upper and lower worlds. The author follows the order of the base text, using each 'قوله' to gloss a phrase sequentially.

Warning Against Probing the Divine Essence
Hashiya explains Quranic verses and warns against probing God's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentary on the verses of blessings and divine essence establishes that human ignorance of self precludes knowledge of God's essence, and therefore one should focus on obedience rather than speculation.

Core Idea
You cannot know Allah's essence because you do not even know yourself.

The commentator explains two Quranic verses and a rhetorical question to drive home a crucial point: our inability to fully comprehend our own state, let alone the Creator's essence. This lesson unpacks the linguistic and theological insights in this passage and their practical implication for the believer.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's words settle before interpreting.
Pay attention to the rhetorical question at the end.
2
Understand the linguistic points
The commentary highlights two linguistic features: 'نعمة' as a singular noun in construct state (مفرد مضاف) implying comprehensiveness, and the superlative 'أحسن' possibly not used in its usual sense. Consider why these points matter for meaning.
These are not mere grammar; they shape the theological message.
3
Grasp the theological conclusion
The passage moves from the impossibility of counting blessings to the imperative of obedience and the prohibition of probing God's essence. The key reason: you are ignorant of yourself, so how can you know your Lord?
This is the central warning: avoid speculation about God's essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وَإِن تَعُدُّوا نِعْمَتَ اللَّهِ لَا تُحْصُوهَا ) (۱) مفرد مضاف؛ أي: قوله : ( فَتَبَارَكَ اللهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخَلِقِينَ ) (۲) : اسم التفضيل ليس على بابه، أو باعتبار الصورة الظاهرية. قوله: (أهذا ينبغي أن يعصى أي من صدرت منه هذه الأفعال العظيمة، التي هي قائمة بك وأنت جاهل بها ولا تدريها، فالواجب عليك أيُّها الشَّخص امتثال أوامره واجتناب نواهيه ولا تجترئ على معرفة ذات خالقك ; فإنَّك جاهل بنفسك فكيف بربك.
His saying: (And if you count the blessings of Allah, you cannot enumerate them) (1) is a singular noun in construct state; meaning: His saying: (So blessed is Allah, the best of creators) (2): the superlative form is not used in its usual sense, or it is with respect to the outward form. His saying: (Is this one who should be disobeyed?) meaning: He from whom these great acts have issued, which are established by you while you are ignorant of them and do not perceive them. So it is incumbent upon you, O person, to comply with His commands and avoid His prohibitions, and do not dare to know the essence of your Creator; for you are ignorant of yourself, so how about your Lord?
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (hashiya) on two Quranic verses and a subsequent rhetorical question from the original text. The author first explains the verse 'إِن تَعُدُّوا نِعْمَتَ اللَّهِ لَا تُحْصُوهَا' by noting that 'نعمة' is a singular noun in construct state (مفرد مضاف), which implies generality and comprehensiveness. Then he comments on 'فَتَبَارَكَ اللهُ أَحْسَنُ الْخَالِقِينَ', stating that the superlative 'أحسن' might not be used in its literal comparative sense but rather indicates the perfection of God's creative act. Finally, he interprets the question 'أهذا ينبغي أن يعصى' as a rhetorical admonition: since all these magnificent acts of creation are manifest through you yet you are ignorant of them, it is absolutely necessary to obey God's commands and refrain from disobedience—and, more importantly, not to presume to investigate the essence of God, because being ignorant of yourself, you cannot comprehend your Lord.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: In fact, the linguistic points serve to emphasize God's infinite blessings and the proper understanding of His attributes, culminating in a strong prohibition against probing the divine essence due to human limitation.

Key Takeaway

The Negative Attributes: Their Precedence and Scope
The author explains why negative attributes are mentioned first and that they are not limited to five.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why negative attributes are mentioned before positive attributes in theology and that they are not limited to five.

Core Idea
Negative attributes purify our conception of God before we adorn it with positive ones.

In this passage, the author explains the logical and pedagogical order of negative and positive attributes. He uses a simple but profound analogy: purification (takhliya) must precede adornment (tahliya). The separation of negative attributes also guards against limiting God's transcendence to just five examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the author's distinction between negative and positive attributes and his analogy of purification and adornment.
2
Understand the analogy
Reflect on why purification comes before adornment in everyday life. How does this apply to our understanding of God?
The author explicitly compares negative attributes to purification.
3
Consider the scope of negative attributes
The author states that negative attributes are not limited to five. Identify the examples he gives and think about why he restricts to five in this text.
He calls the five the 'mothers' of negative attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانياً: الصفات السلبية ( ثم تليها في الذكر (خمسة سلبيَّة) نسبة للسَّلْب؛ أي : النَّفي، إذ مدلول كل واحد منها سلب أمرٍ لا يليق به سبحانه (وهي) أي : الصّفات السَّليَّة . المرتّب على ما قبله والحدوث عليه وعلى صفاته محال. قوله : (أي: النَّفي) : المراد به العدم، إذ السلب والنَّفي والعدم بمعنى واحد، وقدَّم السَّلبيَّة على المعاني ؛ لأنَّ السَّلبيَّة؛ كالتَّخلية بالخاء المعجمة والمعاني؛ كالتَّحلية بالحاء المهملة، والتخلية مقدمة على التحلية . والحقُّ : أنَّ الصِّفات السَّلبيَّة لا تنحصر في هذه الخمسة، إذ من جملتها أنَّه لا ولد له ولا زوجة ولا بسيطاً ولا مركباً، ولا في مكان ولا زمان ولا جهة، وغير ذلك، وإنَّما اقتصر على هذه الخمسة؛ لأنَّها أمها لها ولا والد لها، وهكذا يقال في باقي الصفات. قوله : (إذ مدلول كل واحدة ... إلخ ) : علَّة لقوله : (نسبة للسَّلبيَّة).
Secondly: The negative attributes. Then they follow in mention (five negative ones) relative to negation; i.e., denial, since the meaning of each one of them is the negation of a matter unbefitting Him, exalted. (They are) i.e., the negative attributes, arranged upon what precedes and upon His attributes, impossibility is impossible. His saying: (i.e., denial) means nonexistence, for negation, denial, and nonexistence are synonymous. And he placed the negative before the positive because the negative is like purification (takhliya) and the positive is like adornment (tahliya), and purification precedes adornment. And the truth is that the negative attributes are not confined to these five, for among them are that He has no child, no spouse, is not simple, not composite, not in a place, not in time, not in direction, and other than that. He restricted to these five only because they are their mothers and they have no parent, and so on said for the remaining attributes. His saying: (since the meaning of each one ... etc.) is the cause for his saying: (relative to negation).
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage discusses the negative attributes of God. It begins by stating that there are five negative attributes mentioned after the positive ones, but then it explains the reason for their placement. The author likens the negative attributes to purification (takhliya) and the positive attributes to adornment (tahliya), noting that purification must precede adornment. This analogy clarifies why negative attributes are mentioned first in the text. The passage then asserts that the negative attributes are not limited to these five; they include many others such as having no child, no spouse, not being composite, not being in a place, time, or direction. The reason for restricting to five is that these five are the principal or mother attributes that encompass the rest. The final sentence provides a textual note linking a previous phrase to the meaning of negation.

The Fourth Negative Attribute: Being Unlike Contingent Things
Al-Sawi defines the fourth negative attribute and explains its logical necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the fourth negative attribute (mukhalafat lil-hawadith) and why it is logically entailed by Allah's essential attributes.

Core Idea
Allah is absolutely unlike any created thing in every way.

Al-Sawi now defines the fourth negative attribute: that Allah is different from all contingent beings. This attribute is not arbitrary but follows necessarily from the essential attributes we have already studied. In this passage, he provides a concrete list of what this negation implies, clarifying the precise terminology of substance, body, and accident.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from definition to examples to logical explanation.
Pay attention to the list of negations.
2
Identify the core definition
Find the sentence that states the meaning of the attribute. Understand that it negates any similarity to contingent things.
The definition is: 'عدم الموافقة لشيء من الحوادث'.
3
Examine the list of negations
The passage lists specific things that Allah is not: substance, body, accident, moving, stationary, etc. Note that these are examples of what being 'unlike contingent things' means in practice.
This list is not exhaustive but illustrative.
4
Understand the logical connection
Al-Sawi explains that this attribute is a necessary consequence (لازم) of the essential attributes. He also explains why he mentions it explicitly rather than relying on implication.
The phrase 'عطف اللازم على الملزوم' is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورابع الصفات السَّلبيَّة (تَخَالُفٌ للغير ) أي : مخالفته تعالى لغيره من الحوادث . ومعناها : عدم الموافقة لشيء من الحوادث، فليس تعالى بجوهر ولا جسم ولا عرض ولا متحرّك ولا ساكن ولا يوصف تعالى بالكِبَر ولا بالصِّغَر ، ولا بالفوقية ولا بالتَّحتيَّة ولا بالحلول في الأمكنة.
قوله : (تخالف للغير) عطفه على ما قبله من عطف اللازم على الملزوم، إذ يلزم من وجوب الوجود والقدم والبقاء والقيام بالنفس مخالفته لكل ما سواه تعالى، ولم يكتف بذكر اللازم لما سبق من خطر هذا الفنّ، فلا يكتفى فيه بدلالة الالتزام .
قوله من الحوادث): جمع حادث، وهو الموجود بعد عدم، وهو الجواهر والأعراض.
قوله : ( ولا جسم : هو أخصُّ من الجوهر ، إذ الجسم خاص بالمركب والجوهر الصَّادق به وبالجوهر الفرد.
قوله : ( بالكبر) : أي : الحسي، وأما الكبر المعنوي: بمعنى العظم؛
And the fourth of the negative attributes is (َخَالُفٌ for others), i.e., His being different from other than Him of contingent things. And its meaning is: non-conformity to any contingent thing. So He Most High is not a substance, nor a body, nor an accident, nor moving, nor stationary, nor is He Most High described with bigness nor with smallness, nor with aboveness nor with belowness, nor with indwelling in places. His saying: (opposition for others) is conjoined to what preceded it by the conjunction of the necessary to the necessitated, for it follows from necessity of existence, eternality, everlastingness, and self-subsistence His opposition to everything other than Him Most High, and He did not suffice with mentioning the necessary because of what preceded of the danger of this art, so one does not suffice therein with the indication of implication. His saying: (from contingent things) is the plural of contingent, and it is that which exists after non-existence, and it is substances and accidents. His saying: (and not a body) is more specific than substance, for body is specific to the composite, and substance applies truthfully to it and to the indivisible substance. His saying: (with bigness) i.e., sensory bigness; as for metaphorical bigness, it means greatness.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth negative attribute: مخالفة للحوادث (being unlike contingent things). Al-Sawi first states the attribute itself: 'تخالف للغير' means that Allah Most High is unlike anything other than Him, i.e., all created, contingent beings. Its meaning is that He does not conform to any contingent thing. Consequently, Allah is not a substance (جوهر), nor a body (جسم), nor an accident (عرض), nor moving nor stationary, nor described with sensory bigness or smallness, nor with aboveness or belowness, nor with indwelling in places. This list negates any similarity to created entities. Al-Sawi then explains the grammatical and logical structure. He says the phrase 'تخالف للغير' is conjoined to the previous attributes as 'عطف اللازم على الملزوم' (conjoining the necessary to the necessitated). This means that from the essential attributes of Allah (necessity of existence, eternality, everlastingness, self-subsistence) it necessarily follows that He is different from everything else. The author did not merely mention this consequence because of the gravity of this field—implicit indication (دلالة الالتزام) is not sufficient in kalam. Then he defines 'حوادث' as the plural of 'حادث', which is that which exists after non-existence, i.e., substances and accidents. He clarifies that 'جسم' (body) is more specific than 'جوهر' (substance), because body is limited to composite things while substance includes both composite and simple (indivisible). Finally, he distinguishes 'كبر' (bigness) into sensory (حسي) and metaphorical (معنوي); Allah is negated of sensory bigness but metaphorical bigness (meaning greatness) is affirmed of Him. So the passage establishes a foundational theological principle: Allah is absolutely unlike any created thing, including any spatial or physical attributes.

Key Terms
صفات سلبية
مخالفة للحوادث
جوهر
جسم
عرض
حادث
لازم
ملزوم
دلالة الالتزام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The negations listed (not a body, not above, etc.) are arbitrary or merely scriptural, without logical basis.
Correction: Al-Sawi explicitly states that these negations are logically entailed by the essential attributes of Allah (necessity, eternality, everlastingness, self-subsistence). They are not arbitrary but necessary consequences.

Checkpoint

A) Because it is an essential attribute
B) Because of the danger of this field of knowledge
C) Because it is a positive attribute
D) Because it is derived from revelation

Key Takeaway
The fourth negative attribute, being unlike contingent things, is directly entailed by Allah's necessary existence, eternality, everlastingness, and self-subsistence.

Negation of Sensory Direction
Al-Sawi distinguishes sensory vs. metaphorical aboveness and gives ruling on direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between sensory and metaphorical aboveness and the ruling on believing Allah is in a direction.

Core Idea
Allah is above, but not in a physical location.

Al-Sawi clarifies the negation of direction. He distinguishes sensory aboveness (negated) from metaphorical aboveness (affirmed by Qur'an). He then explains the ruling: belief in a lower direction is disbelief, while belief in an upper direction is sin but not disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on direction
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the distinction between sensory and metaphorical aboveness.
2
Identify the two types of direction beliefs
Find the ruling for belief in a lower direction and for other directions. Why is the lower direction disbelief?
The lower direction implies deficiency.
3
Reflect on the negation
Why does Allah negate sensory direction? How does this protect divine transcendence?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا) بالفوقية :أي الحسيَّة وأمَّا المعنوية : فقد وصف تعالى نفسه بها، قال في كتابه العزيز: (وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ) . والحاصل أنَّ معتقد الجهة فيه ،تفصيل فإن كان جهة السِّفل؛ فهو : كافر لظهور النقص في اعتقاده، وأما غيرها من الجهات؛ فجهل وفسق، ولا يكفّر إلا باعتقاد الحلول.
قوله : (ولا بالحلول في الأمكنة) : أي : وما ورد مما يوهم ذلك فيجب تأويله، ففي الحديث: «ما وسعني أرضي ولا سمائي وإِنَّما وسعني قلب عبدي المؤمن» (١) سورة غافر : (۱۲). (۲) سورة الأنعام: (۱۸). (۳) أورده أبو طالب المكي في قوت القلوب (۲۰۷۱)، وبنحوه أورده الديلمي في الفردوس بمأثور الخطاب» (٤٤٦٦) عن أنس بن مالك له، وأخرجه أحمد في «الزهد (٤٢٣) عن وهب بن منبه قال: (إن الله فتح السماوات لحزقيل حتى نظر إلى العرش - أو كما قال - فقال لحزقيل : سبحانك ما أعظمك يا رب! فقال الله : إن السماوات والأرض لم تطق أن تحملني، وضقن من أن تسعني، ووسعني قلب المؤمن الوادع اللين. وفي الرسالة القشيرية) (۳۷۷/۲) : (وفي بعض الكتب أن موسى قال : يا رب؛ أين تسكن؟ فأوحى الله تعالى إليه : في قلب عبدي المؤمن، ومعناه: سكون الذكر في القلب ؛ فإن الحق الله منزّه عن كل سكون وحلول، وإنما هو إثبات ذكر وتحصيل وينظر إتحاف السادة المتقين (٢٣٤/٧) .
His saying: (and not) with aboveness: i.e., sensory aboveness; as for metaphorical aboveness, He Most High has described Himself with it. He said in His Mighty Book: (And He is the subduer above His servants). And the conclusion is that the believer in direction has a detailed ruling: if it is the direction of below, then he is a disbeliever because of the apparent deficiency in his belief; as for other directions, it is ignorance and sin, and he is not declared a disbeliever except by believing in indwelling. His saying: (and not with indwelling in places): i.e., and whatever is reported that suggests that must be interpreted. For in the hadith: 'My earth and My heavens did not contain Me, but the heart of My believing servant contained Me.' (1) Surah Ghafir: (12). (2) Surah al-An'am: (18). (3) Reported by Abu Talib al-Makki in Qut al-Qulub (2/71), and similarly by al-Daylami in al-Firdaws bi Ma'thur al-Khitab (4466) from Anas ibn Malik, and Ahmad narrated in al-Zuhd (423) from Wahb ibn Munabbih who said: 'Indeed Allah opened the heavens for Hizqil until he saw the Throne – or as he said – so Hizqil said: Glory be to You, how great You are, O Lord! So Allah said: The heavens and earth could not carry Me, and they were too narrow to contain Me, but the heart of the believing, gentle servant contained Me.' And in al-Risala al-Qushayriyya (2/377): 'In some books that Moses said: O Lord, where do You dwell? So Allah Most High revealed to him: In the heart of My believing servant, and its meaning is the stillness of remembrance in the heart; for indeed Allah is exalted above every stillness and indwelling, but it is an affirmation of remembrance and acquisition.' And see It-haf al-Sada al-Muttaqin (7/234).
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage addresses two negations from the list of the fourth attribute: negation of direction (فوقية/تحتية) and negation of indwelling (حلول). For 'فوقية', Al-Sawi distinguishes sensory (حسية) and metaphorical (معنوية) aboveness. Allah negates sensory aboveness (being physically above), but metaphorical aboveness is affirmed as in the Quranic verse: 'وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ' (He is the subduer above His servants). The conclusion (حاصل) is that belief in direction requires distinction: if one believes in a lower direction (جهة السفل), that implies deficiency and thus disbelief (كفر). But belief in any other direction (e.g., above) is ignorance and sin (فسق), not disbelief, unless it leads to believing in indwelling (حلول). For 'حلول', Al-Sawi states that any scriptural text that seems to imply Allah indwells in places must be interpreted (تأويل), because Allah is transcendent. He cites the famous hadith 'ما وسعني أرضي ولا سمائي وإنما وسعني قلب عبدي المؤمن' (My earth and My heavens do not contain Me, but the heart of My believing servant contains Me). This hadith is explained by scholars as referring to the heart's capacity for knowledge and love of Allah, not literal containment. Al-Sawi then provides multiple source references for this hadith and its interpretations, emphasizing that Allah is free from spatial location and that any apparent implication of indwelling is metaphorical. The passage thus defends divine transcendence by insisting on metaphorical interpretation of ambiguous texts.

Key Terms
فوقية
تحتية
جهة
حسي
معنوي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That denying Allah has a direction means He is not truly above or exalted.
Correction: Allah is exalted above His creation, but not in a physical sense; His elevation is metaphorical, denoting supremacy.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a person who believes that Allah is in the direction of below?
A) He is a disbeliever because of the apparent deficiency
B) He is ignorant but not a disbeliever
C) He is a sinner but not a disbeliever
D) He is excused due to ignorance

Key Takeaway
Allah is above His creation in a way that befits His majesty, not in a physical sense.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Negation of Indwelling and Ta'wil
Al-Sawi explains negation of indwelling and necessity of ta'wil, with a hadith example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah cannot indwell places and how texts that suggest indwelling must be interpreted metaphorically.

Core Idea
Allah is too great to be contained by any physical space.

Al-Sawi addresses the negation of indwelling (hulul). He states that any scriptural text seeming to imply Allah's indwelling must be interpreted (ta'wil). He then cites the famous hadith about the heart of the believer containing Allah and explains its true meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on indwelling
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the principle of ta'wil for ambiguous texts.
2
Understand the hadith and its interpretation
The hadith 'My earth and My heavens did not contain Me...' is used. How is it interpreted?
The interpretation is about the heart's capacity for knowledge and love.
3
Reflect on why ta'wil is necessary
Why must such texts be interpreted? How does this protect divine transcendence?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا) بالفوقية :أي الحسيَّة وأمَّا المعنوية : فقد وصف تعالى نفسه بها، قال في كتابه العزيز: (وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ) . والحاصل أنَّ معتقد الجهة فيه ،تفصيل فإن كان جهة السِّفل؛ فهو : كافر لظهور النقص في اعتقاده، وأما غيرها من الجهات؛ فجهل وفسق، ولا يكفّر إلا باعتقاد الحلول.
قوله : (ولا بالحلول في الأمكنة) : أي : وما ورد مما يوهم ذلك فيجب تأويله، ففي الحديث: «ما وسعني أرضي ولا سمائي وإِنَّما وسعني قلب عبدي المؤمن» (١) سورة غافر : (۱۲). (۲) سورة الأنعام: (۱۸). (۳) أورده أبو طالب المكي في قوت القلوب (۲۰۷۱)، وبنحوه أورده الديلمي في الفردوس بمأثور الخطاب» (٤٤٦٦) عن أنس بن مالك له، وأخرجه أحمد في «الزهد (٤٢٣) عن وهب بن منبه قال: (إن الله فتح السماوات لحزقيل حتى نظر إلى العرش - أو كما قال - فقال لحزقيل : سبحانك ما أعظمك يا رب! فقال الله : إن السماوات والأرض لم تطق أن تحملني، وضقن من أن تسعني، ووسعني قلب المؤمن الوادع اللين. وفي الرسالة القشيرية) (۳۷۷/۲) : (وفي بعض الكتب أن موسى قال : يا رب؛ أين تسكن؟ فأوحى الله تعالى إليه : في قلب عبدي المؤمن، ومعناه: سكون الذكر في القلب ؛ فإن الحق الله منزّه عن كل سكون وحلول، وإنما هو إثبات ذكر وتحصيل وينظر إتحاف السادة المتقين (٢٣٤/٧) .
His saying: (and not) with aboveness: i.e., sensory aboveness; as for metaphorical aboveness, He Most High has described Himself with it. He said in His Mighty Book: (And He is the subduer above His servants). And the conclusion is that the believer in direction has a detailed ruling: if it is the direction of below, then he is a disbeliever because of the apparent deficiency in his belief; as for other directions, it is ignorance and sin, and he is not declared a disbeliever except by believing in indwelling. His saying: (and not with indwelling in places): i.e., and whatever is reported that suggests that must be interpreted. For in the hadith: 'My earth and My heavens did not contain Me, but the heart of My believing servant contained Me.' (1) Surah Ghafir: (12). (2) Surah al-An'am: (18). (3) Reported by Abu Talib al-Makki in Qut al-Qulub (2/71), and similarly by al-Daylami in al-Firdaws bi Ma'thur al-Khitab (4466) from Anas ibn Malik, and Ahmad narrated in al-Zuhd (423) from Wahb ibn Munabbih who said: 'Indeed Allah opened the heavens for Hizqil until he saw the Throne – or as he said – so Hizqil said: Glory be to You, how great You are, O Lord! So Allah said: The heavens and earth could not carry Me, and they were too narrow to contain Me, but the heart of the believing, gentle servant contained Me.' And in al-Risala al-Qushayriyya (2/377): 'In some books that Moses said: O Lord, where do You dwell? And see It-haf al-Sada al-Muttaqin (7/234).

Commentary
This passage addresses two negations from the list of the fourth attribute: negation of direction (فوقية/تحتية) and negation of indwelling (حلول). For 'فوقية', Al-Sawi distinguishes sensory (حسية) and metaphorical (معنوية) aboveness. For 'حلول', Al-Sawi states that any scriptural text that seems to imply Allah indwells in places must be interpreted (تأويل), because Allah is transcendent. He cites the famous hadith 'ما وسعني أرضي ولا سمائي وإنما وسعني قلب عبدي المؤمن' (My earth and My heavens do not contain Me, but the heart of My believing servant contains Me). This hadith is explained by scholars as referring to the heart's capacity for knowledge and love of Allah, not literal containment. Al-Sawi then provides multiple source references for this hadith and its interpretations, emphasizing that Allah is free from spatial location and that any apparent implication of indwelling is metaphorical. The passage thus defends divine transcendence by insisting on metaphorical interpretation of ambiguous texts.

Not in a Direction: Physical Above-ness and Below-ness Denied, Metaphorical Above-ness Affirmed
Commentator clarifies negation of physical above-ness/below-ness and gives ruling on direction belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between physical and metaphorical above-ness for Allah and the nuanced ruling on belief in direction: below is kufr, other directions are fisq, and indwelling is kufr.

Core Idea
Allah is not in any physical direction; only metaphorical above-ness is affirmed.

This passage from the commentary on the Kharida addresses a common confusion: when the creed denies 'above-ness' for Allah, does that contradict verses that say He is 'above'? The commentator resolves this by distinguishing physical above-ness (negated) from metaphorical above-ness of rank (affirmed). He then gives the precise ruling for someone who believes Allah is in a direction: a specific ruling for below (kufr) versus other directions (fisq), with indwelling as a separate case of kufr.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the source Arabic once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the flow.
Notice that the passage starts with a line from the matn being commented on.
2
Distinguish physical vs. metaphorical above-ness
The commentator clarifies that 'above-ness' in the negation refers to physical above-ness, while metaphorical above-ness (of rank and power) is affirmed through Quranic evidence.
This resolves an apparent contradiction with verses like 'He is the Subduer above His servants'.
3
Identify the three rulings on direction belief
The passage outlines three cases: belief in below direction (kufr), belief in other directions (fisq), and belief in indwelling (kufr). Understand why each ruling differs.
Below implies deficiency, indwelling implies corporeality—both are incompatible with tawhid.
4
Reflect on the theological nuance
Consider why the commentator distinguishes between physical and metaphorical above-ness, and why the ruling on direction is not simply 'all kufr' but graded.
This reflects a balanced approach that preserves divine transcendence while acknowledging the limits of human understanding.

ولا بالصِّغَر، ولا بالفوقية ولا بالتَّحتيَّة ولا بالحلول في الأمكنة، ولا فهو من أوصافه، قال تعالى: (فَالْحُكْمُ لِلَّهِ الْعَلِي الْكَبِيرِ )
قوله : (ولا) بالفوقية :أي الحسيَّة وأمَّا المعنوية : فقد وصف تعالى نفسه بها، قال في كتابه العزيز: (وَهُوَ الْقَاهِرُ فَوْقَ عِبَادِهِ ) .
والحاصل أنَّ معتقد الجهة فيه تفصيل فإن كان جهة السِّفل؛ فهو : كافر لظهور النقص في اعتقاده، وأما غيرها من الجهات؛ فجهل وفسق، ولا يكفّر إلا باعتقاد الحلول.
Nor by smallness, nor by above-ness nor by below-ness nor by indwelling in places, and nor is He from His attributes, He said: 'Then the judgment belongs to Allah, the Exalted, the Great.' His statement: 'Nor' by above-ness: meaning physical above-ness; as for metaphorical above-ness, He described Himself with it, He said in His Mighty Book: 'And He is the Subduer above His servants.' And the conclusion is that belief in direction is detailed: if it is the direction of below, then he is a disbeliever due to the apparent deficiency in that belief; as for other directions, it is ignorance and sin, and one is not declared a disbeliever except by belief in indwelling.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from the matn of the Kharida that negates from Allah attributes of created beings such as smallness, above-ness, below-ness, and indwelling in places. The commentator first clarifies that the negation of 'above-ness' refers to physical above-ness, but metaphorical above-ness (of rank and power) is affirmed for Allah, as evidenced by the verse 'And He is the Subduer above His servants.' He then summarizes the doctrinal ruling on belief in a specific direction (جهة). If one believes Allah is in the direction of below (i.e., under), that is disbelief because it implies deficiency. Belief in other directions (e.g., above) is ignorance and sin, but not disbelief unless it entails belief in indwelling (حلول), which is also kufr. Thus the passage establishes a nuanced position: affirming direction for Allah is only permissible in a metaphorical sense, and the legal ruling varies depending on the specific belief.

Correction: The passage distinguishes between belief in the direction of below (kufr) and belief in other directions (fisq, not kufr) unless it implies indwelling, which is kufr.

Interpreting the Hadith of Divine Containment
Commentator explains the hadith metaphorically to avoid anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars interpret the hadith about the heart of the believer containing God, safeguarding divine transcendence.

Core Idea
God cannot be contained in space; the hadith refers to remembrance in the heart.

This passage addresses a delicate issue: hadith reports that seem to suggest God dwells in the believer's heart. The commentator insists such texts must be interpreted metaphorically to preserve God's transcendence. We will examine the key hadith and its proper understanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic carefully, noticing how the commentator responds to the hadith.
2
Understand the principle of ta'wil
The commentator states that any text suggesting indwelling must be interpreted. This is the principle of ta'wil for ambiguous attributes.
3
Examine the hadith and its variants
Look at the hadith and the additional reports cited. They reinforce the same point.
4
Learn the correct interpretation
The commentator explains the meaning as 'stillness of remembrance' in the heart, not literal indwelling.
5
Reflect on the theological significance
This interpretation preserves God's transcendence (tanzih) and avoids anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا بالحلول في الأمكنة) : أي : وما ورد مما يوهم ذلك فيجب تأويله، ففي الحديث: «ما وسعني أرضي ولا سمائي وإنَّما وسعني قلب عبدي المؤمن» (٣) (١) سورة غافر : (١٢). (٢) سورة الأنعام: (١٨). (٣) أورده أبو طالب المكي في قوت القلوب (٢٠٧١)، وبنحوه أورده الديلمي في الفردوس بمأثور الخطاب» (٤٤٦٦) عن أنس بن مالك له، وأخرجه أحمد في «الزهد (٤٢٣) عن وهب بن منبه قال: (إن الله فتح السماوات لحزقيل حتى نظر إلى العرش - أو كما قال - فقال لحزقيل : سبحانك ما أعظمك يا رب! فقال الله : إن السماوات والأرض لم تطق أن تحملني، وضقن من أن تسعني، ووسعني قلب المؤمن الوادع اللين. وفي الرسالة القشيرية) (٣٧٧/٢) : (وفي بعض الكتب أن موسى قال : يا رب؛ أين تسكن؟ فأوحى الله تعالى إليه : في قلب عبدي المؤمن، ومعناه: سكون الذكر في القلب ؛ فإن الحق الله منزّه عن كل سكون وحلول، وإنما هو إثبات ذكر وتحصيل وينظر إتحاف السادة المتقين (٢٣٤/٧) .
His statement: 'Nor by indwelling in places': meaning: and whatever is reported that suggests that must be interpreted. So in the hadith: 'My earth and My sky could not contain Me, but the heart of My believing servant contains Me.' (3) [Surah Ghafir: 12; Surah Al-An'am: 18]. (3) Reported by Abu Talib al-Makki in Qut al-Qulub (2071), and similarly by al-Daylami in al-Firdaws bi Ma'thur al-Khitab (4466) from Anas ibn Malik, and Ahmad in al-Zuhd (423) from Wahb ibn Munabbih who said: 'Indeed Allah opened the heavens to Hizqil until he looked at the Throne... then Allah said: The heavens and the earth could not bear to carry Me, and they were too narrow to contain Me, but the heart of the gentle, soft believer contained Me.' And its meaning is: the stillness of remembrance in the heart; for the Truth (Allah) is transcendent above any stillness and indwelling; rather it is an affirmation of remembrance and acquisition.' And see Ittihaf al-Sada al-Muttaqin (7/234).

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the negation of indwelling (حلول في الأمكنة) in the matn. The commentator states that any textual reports that seem to suggest indwelling must be interpreted metaphorically. He then cites the well-known hadith 'My earth and My sky could not contain Me, but the heart of My believing servant contains Me.' The commentator provides the chain and variants of this hadith, including a longer version from Wahb ibn Munabbih. He then quotes from al-Risala al-Qushayriyya, where the question of Moses ('Where do You dwell?') is answered with 'In the heart of My believing servant.' The commentator explains that this means the stillness of remembrance (سكون الذكر) in the heart, not a literal spatial indwelling. Allah is transcendent above any stillness or physical solution. The correct interpretation is that it is an affirmation of remembrance and spiritual presence, not a literal containment. Thus the passage guards against anthropomorphism (tashbih) by insisting on ta'wil of ambiguous texts.

حلول
تأويل
الذكر
سكون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith means God literally dwells inside the believer's body or heart.
Correction: The commentator explains it means the stillness of remembrance (sukun al-dhikr) in the heart, not a physical indwelling.

Key Takeaway
The hadith about the heart containing God must be understood as a reference to the believer's remembrance of God, not as a literal spatial indwelling.

?

But this does not mean God is limited to your heart — rather, your heart is honored by being the place where His remembrance resides. Does the honor of this truth humble you or leave you indifferent? Interpreting 'The Heart is the House of the Lord' – A Metaphor for Divine Mercy
The commentator explains the metaphorical meaning of the hadith about the heart being the house of the Lord.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the metaphorical interpretation of the hadith 'The heart is the house of the Lord' as referring to the locus of God's mercy and self-disclosure, not a literal dwelling.

Core Idea
The heart is not God's literal house; it is the place of His mercy.

This lesson examines a famous hadith that might initially seem to imply that God dwells within the human heart. The commentator clarifies that this is a metaphor. He explains that the hadith actually refers to the heart being the locus of divine mercy and self-disclosure, grounded in humanity's role as bearers of the divine trust.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its interpretation
Read the Arabic passage and translation to see the hadith and the commentator's explanation.
Notice the key terms 'قلب' (heart) and 'بيت الرب' (house of the Lord).
2
Understand the metaphorical shift
The commentator reinterprets 'house of the Lord' as a metaphor for mercy and self-disclosure, not literal indwelling. How does this connect to the earlier hadith about the servant's heart containing God?
The earlier hadith is interpreted as containing awe and mercy, not essence.
3
Connect to the broader theological context
Reflect on how this interpretation upholds divine transcendence while affirming spiritual closeness. The human species bears the trust (أمانة) of obedience.
This affirms that nearness to God is through mercy and obedience, not spatial indwelling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الحديث : «القلبُ بيتُ الرَّبِّ» (١) ، وتأويله أن تقول قوله : وإنَّما وسعني ؛ أي: وسع هيبتي ورحمتي.
وقوله : «القلب بيت الرَّبِّ أي : محلُّ رحمته وتجليه، وذلك لأنَّ النَّوع الإنساني مهبط أوامر الله ونواهيه، إذ هو المتحمّل للأمانة التي عرضت على السَّماوات والأرض فأبين أن يحملنها وأشفقن منها .
And in the hadith: 'The heart is the house of the Lord,' and its interpretation is that you say his statement 'and indeed it contained Me' means: it contained My awe and My mercy. And his statement: 'The heart is the house of the Lord' means: the locus of His mercy and His self-disclosure, and that is because the human species is the place of descent for Allah's commands and prohibitions, since it is the bearer of the trust that was offered to the heavens and the earth, and they refused to carry it and were afraid of it.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the commentary on the theme of indwelling, providing an additional hadith and its interpretation. The commentator cites the hadith 'The heart is the house of the Lord.' He explains that this is a metaphorical expression. The earlier hadith 'My servant's heart contained Me' means it contained God's awe (هيبة) and mercy (رحمة), not His essence. Similarly, 'the heart is the house of the Lord' means it is the locus (محل) of His mercy and self-disclosure (تجلي). The reason is that human beings are the recipients of divine commands and prohibitions, and they bear the trust (أمانة) which the heavens and earth refused. This trust is the responsibility of obedience, and the heart is where this relationship with God is realized. Thus the hadith emphasizes the spiritual nearness of God to the believer, not literal indwelling.

Key Terms
قلب
بيت الرب
رحمة
تجلي
أمانة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the hadith means God literally dwells inside the human heart.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that 'house of the Lord' is a metaphor meaning the heart is the locus of God's mercy and self-disclosure, not a literal dwelling.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what does 'the heart is the house of the Lord' mean?
A) God literally resides in the heart
B) The heart is the locus of God's mercy and self-disclosure
C) The heart is a physical container for God
D) It means the heart is a temple for worship

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'the heart is the house of the Lord' is a metaphor for the heart being the locus of divine mercy and self-disclosure, not a literal dwelling.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of your heart as the place where God’s mercy and awe should dwell, what is the first thing that comes to mind that might be occupying that space instead? What will you do this week to clear it out?
?
The heavens and the earth refused the trust, but you accepted it. Do you truly live with the weight of that responsibility, or have you become complacent? How will you carry it more consciously starting today?
?
If God’s self-disclosure (tajalli) is a real experience of mercy in the heart, when was the last time you felt that? What is one specific change in your daily routine that could help you become more aware of His presence and mercy?

Proof of Allah's Dissimilarity to Created Things
The commentator presents a proof that Allah is unlike created things based on the impossibility of similarity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that Allah is unlike created things, based on the impossibility of shared essential attributes.

Core Idea
If Allah were like His creation, He would share its weakness—but that is impossible.

This lesson presents a concise argument from the Islamic theological tradition for one of Allah's essential attributes: His dissimilarity to everything created. The proof is simple but powerful: if Allah were similar to created things, He would have to share their defining characteristics, such as being brought into existence and being in need. Since those are impossible for the Creator, similarity is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Notice the conditional structure starting with 'law' (if).
2
Identify the conditional argument
The proof is a conditional syllogism. Find the 'if' clause and the 'then' clause. Then note the conclusion that follows from the impossibility of the consequent.
3
Reflect on the importance
This attribute (mukhalafah) is one of the essential attributes of Allah. Think about why establishing dissimilarity is foundational to tawheed.
Without this attribute, the line between Creator and creature would be blurred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل مخالفته تعالى للحوادث
إذ لو كان مماثلاً لها، لوجب له تعالى ما وجب لها من الحدوث والافتقار ، وذلك محال لما مرّ .
قوله : (إذ لو كان مماثلاً لها ... إلخ): شروع في الدليل على المخالفة .
Proof of His being unlike created things: For if He were similar to them, there would necessarily apply to Him what applies to them of origination and need, and that is impossible as previously mentioned. His statement: 'For if He were similar to them... etc.': a beginning of the proof of dissimilarity.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents a concise proof (daleel) for one of the essential attributes of Allah: His dissimilarity to created things (mukhalafatuhu lil hawadith). The proof is an argument by contradiction. If Allah were similar to created, contingent things (al-hawadith), then He would necessarily share their characteristics, specifically being originated (huduth) and being in need (iftiqar) of a creator. But these are impossible for Allah, as has been established earlier (in the discussion about qidam and ghinah). Therefore, Allah cannot be similar to anything created. The commentator then notes that this statement from the matn begins the proof of dissimilarity. The proof is valid because similarity in essence would entail similarity in attributes, and the attributes of contingency are incompatible with divinity.

Key Terms
مخالفة للحوادث
مماثلة
حدوث
افتقار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think similarity only applies to shape or substance, not to essential attributes like origination and need.
Correction: The proof shows that similarity would entail sharing even essential attributes such as being created and being in need, which are impossible for the Creator.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if Allah were similar to created things (hawadith)?
A) He would have a shape
B) He would be originated and in need
C) He would be eternal
D) He would be unlike created things

Key Takeaway
Allah is unlike all created things because sharing their essential attributes would contradict His necessary existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah were similar to creation, He would need things. But He is utterly independent. In what areas of your life do you rely on your own strength, forgetting that you are in constant need of Allah? How can you turn that dependence into worship today?
?
The proof shows that similarity would mean sharing in weakness. Have you ever imagined Allah in a way that limits His perfection — perhaps by comparing Him to a powerful human? What would it take for you to purify your belief so that you only think of Allah as He has described Himself, without any likeness?
?
Since Allah is unlike anything you have ever seen or experienced, your prayers should reflect that awe. The next time you make du'a, stop and remind yourself that you are speaking to the One who has no equal. How does that change the sincerity and humility of your supplication?

Interpreting the Hadith of Divine Nearness: Metaphor, Not Literal Connection
Commentary on negation of connection and interpretation of hadith qudsi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator interprets the sacred hadith about Allah becoming the servant's hearing and sight as a metaphor for overwhelming divine love, not literal union.

Core Idea
When Allah 'becomes' the servant's senses, it is a metaphor for love so deep that only God is witnessed.

This lesson examines a key sacred hadith that might seem to suggest God is connected to human faculties. The commentator Sanusi (via al-Sawi) explains that such texts must be interpreted metaphorically. He teaches that the hadith describes a state where divine love overwhelms the servant, making him independent of witnessing anything other than God. Understanding this protects against literalist errors like indwelling (hulul) or union (ittihad).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the commentator's immediate assertion that any text suggesting connection must be interpreted (mu'awwal).
This sets the principle: ambiguous texts need interpretation.
2
Identify the hadith and its interpretation
Locate the sacred hadith (hadith qudsi) and the commentator's interpretation. The key term is 'kinaaya' (metaphor).
The interpretation is that it describes the overwhelming (istila') of God's love.
3
Reflect on why this interpretation is necessary
Consider why the commentator insists on metaphorical interpretation: to protect divine transcendence (tanzih) and avoid anthropomorphism or union (ittihad).
This is a core principle of Sunni theology.
4
Connect to broader lesson on ambiguous texts
Think about how this method applies to other scriptural verses that might suggest physical attributes or location for Allah.
Ahl al-Sunna always interpret such texts in a way befitting Allah's majesty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا بالاتصال... إلخ) : أي : ما ورد مما يوهم الاتصال مؤوّل، ففي الحديث القدسي : ولا يزال عبدي يتقرَّبُ إليَّ بالنوافل حتَّى أحبَّه، فإذا أحببته؛ كنتُ سمعه الذي يسمع به، وبصره الذي يُبصر به، ورِجْلَه التي يمشي بها ، ويده التي يبطش بها (۲)، وتأويله : أنَّ ذلك كناية عن استيلاء محبَّة الله على الشَّخص حتّى أغنته عن شهود سواه.
His statement: 'Nor by connection... etc.': meaning: whatever is reported that suggests connection must be interpreted. So in the sacred hadith: 'My servant continues to draw near to Me with voluntary acts until I love him, and when I love him, I become his hearing with which he hears, his sight with which he sees, his leg with which he walks, and his hand with which he strikes.' (2) And its interpretation is that it is a metaphor for the overwhelming of the person by the love of God until it makes him independent of witnessing other than Him.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the negation of connection (اتصال) and other spatial relations from Allah. The commentator states that any texts suggesting a literal connection must be interpreted metaphorically. He then cites the famous sacred hadith (hadith qudsi) wherein Allah says that when a servant draws near through voluntary acts, Allah becomes his hearing, sight, leg, and hand. The commentator interprets this as a metaphor (kinaaya) for the overwhelming (istila') of divine love upon the person, such that he is so absorbed in God that he is no longer aware of his own self or other beings. It does not mean a literal union or indwelling; rather it describes a state of spiritual proximity and love. Thus the passage guards against any literal understanding of connection or union (ittihad).

Key Terms
اتصال
حديث قدسي
كناية
استيلاء المحبة
شهود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some take the hadith literally, thinking God physically becomes the servant's senses or indwells him.
Correction: The commentator clarifies it is a metaphor for the overwhelming of God's love, not literal union.

Checkpoint
How does the commentator interpret the hadith 'I become his hearing, his sight...'?
A) As a literal transformation of God into human senses
B) As a metaphor for the overwhelming of the person by God's love
C) As a proof of indwelling (hulul)
D) As a description of physical union

Key Takeaway
This hadith is a metaphor for the overwhelming love of God that causes the servant to see only Him, not a literal connection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever experienced a moment when your awareness of God was so intense that you forgot your own existence and everything around you? What would need to change in your daily routine to make that a more frequent reality?
?
The commentator says the servant is made 'independent of witnessing other than Him.' What are the 'others'—people, possessions, ambitions—that you are still addicted to witnessing? Name one you are unwilling to let go of, and ask yourself why.
?
If this hadith describes overwhelming love as a goal, what is the biggest barrier in your heart that prevents you from feeling that love right now? What one step will you take today to remove it?
