The Hadith on Vision of Allah in the Resurrection Grounds
Al-Sawi cites a hadith and interprets it to support ru'yah for believers before Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a hadith cited by al-Sawi supports the occurrence of ru'yah (vision of Allah) for believers in the resurrection grounds and how the Salaf interpret the verse about 'uncovering the shin.'

Core Idea
The vision of Allah occurs not only in Paradise but also in the resurrection grounds for believers.

Al-Sawi cites a detailed hadith describing events on the Day of Judgment to support the view that believers will see Allah in the resurrection grounds before entering Paradise. This hadith addresses the testing of believers and hypocrites through successive manifestations. Understanding this hadith clarifies an important point in Islamic eschatology: the vision of Allah (ru'yah) is granted to believers even before Paradise.

Guided Path
1
Read the full hadith narrative
Begin by reading the entire hadith as presented in the Arabic passage. Notice the sequence of events: the call, the destruction of false worshippers, the remaining community, the tests with angels, and the final manifestation of Allah.
The hadith is lengthy but forms a coherent story.
2
Identify the test for believers and hypocrites
Focus on how the believers recognize the true Lord despite the angelic impostors. The hypocrites fail to prostrate when Allah manifests.
This highlights a key difference between sincere believers and hypocrites.
3
Connect to the Quranic verse
Al-Sawi links the hadith to the verse 'Yawma yukshafu ʿan sāq' (The Day the shin shall be uncovered). Note how he explains the Salaf's metaphorical interpretation.
This connection reinforces the hadith's authenticity and interpretation.
4
Understand the doctrinal conclusion
End by affirming that the Sunnah indicates ru'yah occurs in the resurrection grounds for believers, which is the correct view according to al-Sawi.
This is the main takeaway: ru'yah is not limited to Paradise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع قوله : (ففي السُّنَّة ما يقتضي وقوعها فيها للمؤمنين أيضاً) أي: لما ورد في الحديث ما معناه: ينادي مناد من قبل الله تعالى يوم القيامة : كلُّ أمَّة تتّبع معبودها، فعباد الشَّمس يلقون معها في النَّار، وهكذا كلُّ معبودِ عابده إِلَّا مَن مَّنَّ الله، كعيسى، ومريم، وعلي ؛ فإنَّ من عبدهم يلقى مع شيطانه في النَّار ... إلى أن قال في الحديث: «فتبقى هذه الأمة وفيها منافقوها، فيقولون: لا نبرح حتّى نرى معبودنا، فيتجلى لهم ملك لو وضعت بحار الأرض في نقرة إبهامه لوسعها، فيقول لهم: أنا ربُّكم امتحاناً لهم، فيقولون: نعوذ بالله لست ربَّنا؛ فإنَّ ربَّنا لا يتحيّز وأنت متحيز ؛ ثم يتجلى لهم ملك آخر لو وضعت بحار الأرض ومثلها معها في نقرة إبهامه لوسعها، فيقولون له مثل ما قالوا للأول، ثمَّ يتجلَّى الله ، فيخرُّ المؤمنون سجَّداً، فيريد المنافقون السُّجود كالمؤمنين، فلا يقدرون؛ لأنه يصير ظهوره مطبقاً ، فينادى المنادي : (وَامْتَرُوا الْيَوْمَ أَيُّهَا الْمُجْرِمُونَ )) وهذا معنى قوله تعالى: (يَوْمَ يُكْشَفُ عَن سَاقٍ... الآية) ، فكشف الساق عند الخلف مؤوّل بكشف الحجاب، أو كما قال . وقولي : في جنَّة الخُلد وأمّا في عَرَصَات القيامة؛ ففي السُّنَّة ما يقتضي وقوعها فيها للمؤمنين أيضاً وهو الصحيح.
With His statement: (In the Sunnah is what necessitates its occurrence in it for the believers as well), meaning: because there came in the hadith its meaning: A caller calls from before Allah Almighty on the Day of Resurrection: Every nation follows its object of worship. So the worshippers of the sun are thrown with it into the Fire, and likewise every object of worship with its worshipper, except those upon whom Allah has bestowed favor, such as Jesus, Mary, and Ali. Indeed, whoever worshipped them is thrown with his devil into the Fire... until he said in the hadith: 'Then this nation remains, and among them are its hypocrites. They say: We will not depart until we see our object of worship. Then a king appears to them who, if the seas of the earth were placed in the hole of his thumb, they would fit. He says to them: I am your Lord, testing them. They say: We seek refuge with Allah, you are not our Lord, for our Lord is not confined and you are confined. Then another king appears to them who, if the seas of the earth and the like of them were placed in the hole of his thumb, they would fit. They say to him the same as they said to the first. Then Allah manifests, and the believers fall down prostrating. The hypocrites want to prostrate like the believers, but they cannot, because His manifestation becomes overwhelming. Then the caller calls: (Separate yourselves today, O criminals!).' And this is the meaning of His statement: (The Day the shin shall be uncovered... the verse). So the uncovering of the shin according to the Salaf is interpreted as the unveiling of the veil, or as he said. And I say: In the Garden of Eternity, but as for the resurrection grounds, in the Sunnah is what necessitates its occurrence in them for the believers as well, and it is the correct view.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from the main text that states the Sunnah implies the occurrence of ru'yah (vision of Allah) for believers in the resurrection grounds (ʿaraṣāt al-qiyāma) as well. The commentator, al-Sawi, begins by explaining this line: he cites a lengthy hadith describing events of the Day of Judgment. In this hadith, a call is made for each nation to follow its object of worship; the worshippers of the sun and other false deities are thrown into the Fire with their objects, except those whom Allah has protected, such as those who worshipped Jesus, Mary, or Ali (these are mentioned as examples of those who were worshipped improperly). Then the hadith continues: the believing community remains with its hypocrites. They refuse to move until they see their object of worship. Two different angels appear in succession, each claiming to be the Lord, but the believers recognize them as created beings because they are confined in space. Finally, Allah manifests, and the believers prostrate. The hypocrites attempt to prostrate but fail, and a voice separates the criminals. Al-Sawi then connects this to the Quranic verse 'Yawma yukshafu ʿan sāq' (the Day the shin is uncovered) and notes that the Salaf interpret 'kashf al-sāq' as the removal of the veil, not a literal shin. After explaining the hadith, al-Sawi concludes by affirming that ru'yah indeed occurs in the resurrection grounds for believers, and this is the correct view.

Key Terms
رؤية الله
عرصات القيامة
كشف الساق
تجلي
منافقون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ru'yah only occurs in Paradise for believers.
Correction: A hadith and its interpretation by al-Sawi show that ru'yah also occurs in the resurrection grounds.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what happens when Allah manifests on the Day of Judgment?
A) All people prostrate, including hypocrites.
B) Only the believers prostrate; hypocrites cannot.
C) No one prostrates until after entering Paradise.
D) The believers prostrate but hypocrites flee.

Key Takeaway
The hadith cited by al-Sawi affirms that believers will see Allah in the resurrection grounds before entering Paradise, and the term 'kashf al-sāq' is interpreted metaphorically by the Salaf.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hypocrites in the hadith wanted to see their object of worship but could not because their hearts were insincere. Are you truly seeking Allah in this life, or are you just going through the motions? What would happen if Allah manifested His glory to you today—would you fall in prostration or find yourself unable?
?
The believers recognized the true Lord because He is not confined or limited to space. Do you sometimes confine Allah in your mind by imagining Him in human-like terms or limiting His attributes? What step can you take today to purify your understanding of His transcendence?
?
The hadith describes a test of seeing Allah in the resurrection grounds. How does the hope of seeing your Lord in the Hereafter affect how you live your life right now? Write one concrete intention you will act on to prepare for that moment.

Disbelievers Do Not See Allah on the Day of Judgment
Al-Sawi refutes the claim that disbelievers see Allah, quoting the verse of hijab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic proof that disbelievers are veiled from Allah on the Day of Judgment and why the presence of hypocrites does not imply they see Him.

Core Idea
The Quranic veil is decisive: disbelievers are veiled and do not see Allah.

Some have claimed that even disbelievers, particularly hypocrites, will see Allah on the Day of Judgment. Al-Sawi addresses this claim head-on by quoting a powerful Quranic verse and explaining why the physical crowding of hypocrites with believers does not mean they share in the vision. This lesson clarifies the doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the objection 'some say' and the refutation that follows.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
Al-Sawi quotes the verse 'Kalla innahum 'an rabbihim yawma'idhin lamahjubun'. Understand that this is the main evidence that disbelievers are veiled.
The verse is from Surah al-Mutaffifin (83:15).
3
Analyze the counterargument
The objector might say that hypocrites are present among believers, so they should see. Al-Sawi responds that presence does not cause vision; their actions are mere imitation.
The key term is 'taqlid' (imitation).
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why this matters: it preserves the honor of the vision for believers only and upholds divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بل قيل : وللكفار أي والمنافقين، لكنَّ الحقَّ أنَّهم لم يروا لقوله تعالى: كَلَّا إِنَّهُمْ عَن رَّبِّهِمْ يَوْمَدٍ مَحْجُوبُونَ، ولا يلزم من مزاحمة المنافقين للمؤمنين في القيامة رؤيته، وإنَّما قولهم وفعلهم تقليد كما كانوا يفعلونه في الدُّنيا .
Rather it is said: and for the disbelievers, i.e., the hypocrites. But the truth is that they did not see Him, due to His statement: 'No indeed, on that Day they will be veiled from their Lord.' And it does not follow from the crowding of the hypocrites with the believers at the resurrection that they see Him; rather their speech and action is imitation as they used to do in the world.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its refutation. Some have claimed that disbelievers, specifically the hypocrites, will also see Allah on the Day of Judgment. Al-Sawi rejects this by appealing to the Quranic verse (Surah al-Mutaffifin 83:15): 'Kalla innahum 'an rabbihim yawma'idhin lamahjubun' (No indeed, on that Day they will be veiled from their Lord). This verse directly states that the disbelievers are veiled, so they cannot see Allah. The commentator then addresses a potential counterargument: the hypocrites are physically present among the believers during the manifestation, so one might think they also see Allah. Al-Sawi explains that this does not follow. Their physical presence does not imply vision; rather, their words and actions are mere imitation (taqlid) of the believers, just as they used to pretend in the worldly life. Thus, the objection is invalid.

Key Terms
حجب
منافقون
تقليد
مزاحمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because hypocrites are physically present with believers during the vision of Allah, they also see Him.
Correction: The Quranic verse says they are veiled, and their presence is only imitation (taqlid), not actual vision.

Checkpoint
What is the main proof al-Sawi uses to argue that disbelievers do not see Allah on the Day of Judgment?
A) A hadith about the hypocrites.
B) The consensus of the scholars.
C) The Quranic verse about being veiled.
D) Logical reasoning about divine transcendence.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse of hijab decisively proves that disbelievers are veiled from seeing Allah on the Day of Judgment, and their presence among believers does not imply vision.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there areas in your life where you are merely imitating the outward actions of believers—praying, fasting, giving charity—without the inner faith that transforms those actions into true worship? What would it take for you to move from taqlid to sincere faith?
?
The hypocrites will be veiled from Allah on the Day of Judgment despite their physical presence among the believers. How does this reality weigh on your heart when you consider those around you who appear Muslim but may lack genuine conviction? What are you doing to ensure your own faith is not merely a show?
?
If you knew that one day you might be physically present among the righteous yet separated from Allah by a veil, how would you change your priorities today to ensure that your actions are not just imitation but born from a living relationship with your Lord?

Seeing Allah in Dreams: Reality and Types
Al-Sawi discusses the reality and types of seeing Allah in dreams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reality of seeing Allah in dreams as a heart-vision, with the example of Imam Ahmad and the classification of visions.

Core Idea
Dream visions of Allah are heart-visions, not literal eye sightings.

Al-Sawi addresses a topic that often raises questions: can believers see Allah in dreams? He affirms it has occurred for many righteous people and clarifies that such visions are spiritual, not physical. To illustrate, he recounts a famous incident from Imam Ahmad's life, and then begins to classify the types of visions. Let's examine the passage carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that al-Sawi affirms the occurrence of seeing Allah in dreams and immediately clarifies its nature.
The Arabic uses 'mushāhada qalbiyya' (heart-vision).
2
Understand the nature of this vision
Al-Sawi states it is a type of observation with the heart, not the eye. This is crucial: it distinguishes dream visions from the physical seeing of Allah in the afterlife.
3
Analyze the story of Imam Ahmad
The story illustrates the value of Quran recitation. Note that Imam Ahmad asked about the best act of worship and was told to recite Allah's speech, whether with understanding or without. This shows the importance of consistent recitation.
The phrase 'bi-fahm wa bi-ghayri fahm' means both with and without understanding.
4
Identify the two modes of vision
Al-Sawi begins a classification: when seen in a dream, Allah may appear with the description mentioned in the book of Tawhid (true) or with attributes of contingent beings (symbolic). The passage cuts off, but this classification helps interpret visions.
The second type requires interpretation, as the dreamer may be seeing a symbolic representation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما رؤيته تعالى في المنام فقد وقعت لكثير من الصَّالحين من سلف الأمّة وخَلَفهم، ولا خفاء في أنّها نوع مشاهدة تكون بالقلب لا بالعين . قوله : (وأما رؤيته تعالى في المنام فقد وقعت . . . إلخ): من جملة من رآه في المنام الإمام أحمد بن حنبل، فقد نقل عنه : أنه رآه في المنام تسعة وتسعين مرَّةً، وقال : لئن رأيته تمام المئة ؛ لأسألنَّه عن أفضل ما يتقرَّب به المتقربون، فرآه تمام المئة، وسأله فقال له : (بتلاوة كلامي يا أحمد)، فقال : بفهم وبغير فهم؟ فقال: (بفهم وبغير فهم) . واعلم أنَّه إذا رئي في المنام؛ فقد يرى بالصفة التي ذكرت في : التوحيد وهي حقٌّ، وقد يرى بصفة الحوادث؛ فإنَّ رئي كذلك وأمر الرَّائي...
And as for seeing Him, may He be exalted, in a dream, it has occurred to many of the righteous from the predecessors and successors of the community, and there is no concealment that it is a type of vision that occurs with the heart, not with the eye. His saying: 'And as for seeing Him in a dream...': Among those who saw Him in a dream was Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal. It is narrated from him that he saw Him in a dream ninety-nine times, and he said: If I see Him the full hundred, I will ask Him about the best means by which the seekers draw near. So he saw Him the full hundred and asked Him, and He said: 'By reciting My speech, O Ahmad.' He said: With understanding or without? He said: 'With understanding and without.' And know that when He is seen in a dream, He may be seen with the description mentioned in the book of Tawhid, and that is true, and He may be seen with the description of contingent beings. If He is seen thus, and the dreamer...
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage discusses the topic of seeing Allah (ru'yah) in dreams, which is distinct from the vision in the afterlife. Al-Sawi begins by affirming that such visions have occurred for many righteous people, both among the early generations (salaf) and later ones (khalaf). He then clarifies the nature of this vision: it is a type of spiritual observation (mushāhada) that occurs with the heart, not with the physical eye. To illustrate, he narrates a well-known story about Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, a prominent Sunni scholar. Imam Ahmad saw Allah in a dream ninety-nine times and resolved that if he saw Him a hundred times, he would ask about the best act of worship. When he did see Him the hundredth time, he asked, and Allah replied: 'By reciting My speech, O Ahmad.' When Imam Ahmad asked whether this should be done with understanding or without, the answer was: 'With understanding and without.' This highlights the importance of Quran recitation regardless of understanding. Finally, al-Sawi provides a classification: when Allah is seen in a dream, it can be in two ways. First, He may be seen in a manner described in the book of Tawhid—i.e., with attributes befitting His majesty—and this is true. Second, He may be seen in a manner resembling contingent beings (ṣifat al-ḥawādith). If He is seen like that, the dreamer... (the text cuts off, likely explaining that such a dream requires interpretation).

Key Terms
رؤية المنام
مشاهدة قلبية
الإمام أحمد بن حنبل
توحيد
صفة الحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think dreaming of Allah is impossible or that it is always a literal physical sighting.
Correction: Al-Sawi clarifies that such visions occur for the righteous and are heart-visions, not physical eye sightings. They can be either true (with proper attributes) or symbolic (with attributes of contingent beings).

Checkpoint
According to al-Sawi, what is the nature of seeing Allah in a dream?
A) It is a physical vision with the eyes.
B) It is a vision that occurs with the heart, not the eye.
C) It is only for prophets.
D) It is impossible and delusional.

Key Takeaway
Seeing Allah in dreams is a spiritual heart-vision experienced by saints; while some visions are true representations, others are symbolic and require interpretation.

?

?

?
The passage says some dream visions are true and others are symbolic. Have you ever dismissed a dream as meaningless without considering it might be a sign from Allah? How will you approach your dreams from now on, seeking guidance and reflection?

Refutation of Ibn al-Farid's Claim to See Allah
Sawi refutes Ibn al-Farid's poetic claim of seeing Allah while awake.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sawi refutes the claim of seeing Allah while awake and the ruling that such a claim constitutes disbelief.

Core Idea
Claiming to see Allah in this world is kufr, even for a Sufi poet.

This lesson addresses a famous objection based on the poetry of Ibn al-Farid, which seems to imply that he saw Allah with his physical eyes. While some may view such poetry as spiritually lofty, the theological stance is clear: any claim of seeing Allah in this life goes against the Quranic verse 'You shall not see Me' and is considered disbelief. We will examine the objection and the ruling given by Sawi.

Guided Path
1
Read the poetic lines carefully.
The objector quotes three lines from Ibn al-Farid that appear to describe seeing Allah. Read them and note the key phrases about sight and 'lan tarani'.
2
Understand the objection.
The objector asks how to deal with these verses given that they suggest actual vision of Allah.
3
Learn the answer.
Sawi replies that even if the intended meaning is actual vision, the claimant is a disbeliever according to one opinion. This shows the seriousness of the matter.
4
Reflect on the implication.
Consider why such a strong ruling exists and how it guards divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن قلت : كيف تصنع في قول العارف ابن الفارض : [من الكامل] وأباح طرفي نظرةً أملتها فغدوتُ معروفاً وكنت مُنَكَّراً وقوله أيضاً : [من الكامل] وإذا سألتك أن أراك حقيقةً فاسمح ولا تجعل جوابي لن ترى وقوله أيضاً : [من الطويل] لذَّتِ ومنَّ على سمعي بلن إن منعت أن أراك فمن قبلي لغيري أنَّ مقصوده رؤية الله وأنَّه رأى بالفعل، مع أنه من ادعى ذلك؛ فهو كافر على أحد القولين.
If you say: How do you deal with the saying of the gnostic Ibn al-Farid: [al-Kamil] 'My sight permitted a glance I hoped for, so I became known after being unknown' and his saying also: [al-Kamil] 'And if I ask You to let me see You truly, then be generous and do not make my answer 'You shall not see'' and his saying also: [al-Tawil] 'You favored me and bestowed upon my hearing 'lan' (never); if You prevent me from seeing You, then from before me it was for others [to hear]' — [The answer is] that his intended meaning is the vision of God and that he actually saw, but whoever claims that is a disbeliever according to one of the two opinions.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objector quotes three lines of poetry from the famous Sufi poet Ibn al-Farid that seem to claim he saw Allah. The first line says 'my sight permitted a glance' implying physical sight. The second asks to 'see You truly' and references the Quranic response 'lan tarani' (You shall not see Me). The third mentions being granted 'lan' (never) in hearing, and that if prevented from seeing, it was for others. The objector asks how to reconcile these verses with the doctrine that no one sees Allah in this world. The answer is that even if Ibn al-Farid's intended meaning was actual vision, claiming such a thing makes one a disbeliever according to one of the two scholarly opinions. Thus, the poetry is either misinterpreted or the claim is heretical.

Key Terms
ابن الفارض
الرؤية
يقظة
كافر
العارف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Sufi poetry implying vision of Allah is acceptable and not problematic.
Correction: However, the passage shows that if taken literally as a claim of physical sight of Allah while awake, it is considered disbelief.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on someone who claims to have seen Allah with physical eyes while awake, according to this passage?
A) He is a saint.
B) He is a disbeliever according to one of the two opinions.
C) He is excused because of his spiritual station.
D) He is merely mistaken but not sinful.

Key Takeaway
Claiming to have seen Allah with physical eyes in this world is an act of disbelief according to one scholarly opinion, even if expressed in poetic form.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been drawn to a beautiful expression of faith that contradicts clear theological truths? What would you sacrifice—your intellectual integrity or your emotional comfort—if faced with such a contradiction?
?
If you were to encounter a respected spiritual figure making a claim that amounts to kufr, would you have the courage to reject it publicly? Or would your loyalty to the person outweigh your loyalty to Allah?

The Sunni Position on Seeing Allah in This World
Al-Sawi explains the Sunni position on ru'ya and refutes claims of physical sight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on seeing Allah in this world, including the debate between Aisha and Ibn Abbas, and the severe warning against claiming physical sight.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah with physical eyes in this world is impossible; those who claim it are misguided.

This passage from Al-Sawi clarifies an important Sunni doctrine: Allah cannot be seen with physical eyes in this world. It addresses the views of Aisha and Ibn Abbas, and uses the examples of Moses and Prophet Muhammad to illustrate the supremacy of vision over speech. The lesson ends with a strong warning against those who claim such vision.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context of the debate
The passage begins by stating that seeing Allah is not only with the heart. Al-Sawi explains that this phrase refers to the view of Aisha, who denied physical sight, but Ibn Abbas affirmed it. The principle of 'affirmant over negator' is invoked.
Aisha's view is that vision is only of the heart; Ibn Abbas allows it in the hereafter.
2
Examine the case of Moses and Muhammad
Moses was given speech (kalām), not vision; he is called Kalīm. Prophet Muhammad was also given speech but attained vision, which is more noble, so he is not called Kalīm.
3
Grasp the severe warning
Whoever claims to have seen Allah with physical eyes while awake is misguided and misleads others, with some saying he is a sinner or apostate.
This warning emphasizes the seriousness of the claim.
4
Apply the lesson
Recognize that any claim of physical vision of Allah in this world contradicts Sunni theology. The passage provides a clear criterion for orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام على رؤية الله تعالى لا بالقلب فقط . وقوله : (لا بالقلب فقط ) : هو قول السيدة عائشة، ورجح قول ابن عباس؛ بأنَّه مثبت وهو مقدَّم على النافي، على أنَّها لم تدرك زمنها ولم تقع في الدُّنيا لغيره الله، وأمَّا الكليم فلم ير، وإنَّما حصل له الكلام وهو أعظم عطاياه، فسمى كليماً ولم يسمَّى النَّبيُّ كليماً ، أُعطي الكلام أيضاً ؛ لكونه فاز بالأشرف وهو الرُّؤية، فمن ادعى رؤية الله يقظة بعيني رأسه ؛ فهو ضال مضل، قيل : فاسق، وقيل : مرتد .
The discussion on seeing Allah Almighty, not only with the heart. And his saying: '(not only with the heart)': that is the saying of Lady Aisha, and he gave preponderance to the saying of Ibn Abbas because he is an affirmant and the affirmant is given precedence over the negator, and that she did not witness her time, and it did not occur in the world for other than Allah. As for the Kalim (Moses), he did not see, rather he received speech which is his greatest gift, so he was called Kalim and the Prophet (Muhammad) was not called Kalim, although he was given speech as well, because he attained the more noble (vision). So whoever claims to have seen Allah awake with his eyes, he is a misguided misleader; it is said he is a sinner, and it is said he is an apostate.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage defines the doctrinal position on seeing Allah (ru'ya) in this world. It begins by stating the issue: Allah is not seen only with the heart, meaning that the vision is not merely mental. The author then explains the phrase 'not only with the heart' as being the view of Aisha, who denied the possibility of physical sight of Allah in this world. Ibn Abbas affirmed it, and the author gives preponderance to Ibn Abbas because the affirmant (muthbit) is preferred over the negator (nafi). However, he notes that Aisha did not live in the time of the Prophet's ascension (or did not witness the event), and that such vision did not occur for anyone other than Allah. He then mentions Moses (the Kalim), who did not see Allah but received speech, which is his great gift; thus he is called Kalim. The Prophet Muhammad was also given speech, but he is not called Kalim because he attained the more noble gift: vision (ru'ya). The passage concludes with a strong warning: whoever claims to have seen Allah with his physical eyes while awake is a misguided misleader; some say he is a sinner, others say he becomes an apostate.

Correction: The passage distinguishes between heart-vision and physical sight, and explicitly warns that claiming physical sight of Allah in this world is a sign of misguidance and can be considered apostasy.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position is that Allah cannot be seen with physical eyes in this world; any claim to such vision is a sign of misguidance and may constitute apostasy.

How often do you find yourself inclined to deny or doubt what you haven't experienced? Will you seek to affirm the truth from revelation, even when it challenges your limited perception?
?
The Prophet Muhammad attained the noblest gift of vision, yet he never claimed to see Allah with his physical eyes in this world. Are you chasing a spiritual 'high' or miraculous sight instead of the true means of nearness to Allah—listening to His speech (the Quran) and following His command? Interpreting Ibn al-Farid's Poetry on Seeing Allah
Al-Sawi gives two allegorical interpretations of Ibn al-Farid's poetry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Sawi defends the Sunni doctrine that Allah cannot be seen in this world by interpreting Ibn al-Farid's poetry allegorically—either as addressed to the Prophet or as referring to heart-vision.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Farid's poetry uses allusion, not literal claims about seeing Allah.

Some Sufi poetry may appear to contradict the clear Sunni position that Allah cannot be physically seen in this world. Al-Sawi addresses this by showing that the verses of the renowned poet Ibn al-Farid are either addressed to the Prophet Muhammad or refer to an inner, spiritual vision of the heart. This lesson unpacks his method and helps you see how kalam scholars handle such objections from poetic sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and poetry lines
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the objector cites three different lines from Ibn al-Farid that seem to claim that the poet saw Allah.
The lines use phrases like 'permitted my eye a glance' and 'if I ask You to see You truly'.
2
Identify the first answer — prophetic address
Al-Sawi's first answer interprets the poetry as addressing the Prophet, not Allah. Trace how he connects 'lan' (never) to the story of Moses and reinterprets the request for vision as a request to the Prophet to show his essence.
Notice the shift: the poet is asking the Prophet to treat him differently from Moses.
3
Identify the second answer — heart-vision
The second answer interprets 'vision' as heart-vision (ru'ya qalbiyya). The word 'eye' becomes a metaphor for the heart. See how this preserves divine transcendence while honoring the poet's spiritual experience.
Al-Sawi emphasizes that the poetry is not explicit about the Supreme Essence; it uses allusion (kinaaya).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن قلت : كيف تصنع في قول العارف ابن الفارض : [من الكامل] وأباح طرفي نظرةً أملتها فغدوتُ معروفاً وكنت مُنَكَّراً وقوله أيضاً : [من الكامل] وإذا سألتك أن أراك حقيقةً فاسمح ولا تجعل جوابي لن ترى وقوله أيضاً : [من الطويل] لذَّتِ ومنَّ على سمعي بلن إن منعت أن أراك فمـن قـبـلـي لـغـيـري أنَّ مقصوده رؤية الله وأنَّه رأى بالفعل، مع أنه من ادعى ذلك؛ فهو كافر على أحد القولين . قلت أحسن ما يجاب به ؛ أنَّ ذلك خطاب للحضرة النبوية، فقوله: (ومن عـلـى سـمـعي ... إلخ؛ أي: يا رسول الله ؛ إن لـم تـرنـي ذاتك فأسمعني خطابك، وقوله : (وإذا سألتك . . . ( إلخ؛ أي: يا رسول الله ؛ لا تعاملني في رؤيتك كما عومل به موسى بل عاملني في رؤيتك وأرني ذاتك، كما أراك الله ذاته . ولذا قال أيضاً : [من الخفيف] أبق لي مقلةً لـعـلـي يــومـاً قبل موتي أرى بـهـا مـن رآكـا ويجاب أيضاً بأنَّ الكلام في الحضرة الإلهية، والرُّؤية محمولة على الرُّؤية القلبية التي قال فيها : [ من الطويل] أنلنا مع الأحباب رؤيتك الَّتي إليها قلوب الأولياء تسارع فقوله: (وأباح طرفي أي قلبي وسماه طرفاً تجوزاً ؛ لأنَّ الكلام خارج مخرج الكناية؛ لأنه ليس صريحاً في الذات العليَّة .
If you say: How do you deal with the saying of the gnostic Ibn al-Farid: [from al-Kamil] 'He permitted my eye a glance that I desired, so I became known after being unknown' and his saying also: [from al-Kamil] 'And if I ask You to see You truly, be generous and do not make my answer 'You will not see'' and his saying also: [from al-Tawil] 'He favored my hearing with 'lan' (never) if he prevented me from seeing You, so from before me to others' that his intention is seeing Allah and that he saw actually, even though whoever claims that is a disbeliever according to one of the two opinions. I say: The best answer is that that is an address to the prophetic presence. So his saying: 'And He favored my hearing...' means: O Messenger of Allah, if you do not show me Your essence, then make me hear Your speech. And his saying: 'And if I ask You...' means: O Messenger of Allah, do not treat me in my vision of You as Moses was treated, but treat me in my vision and show me Your essence, just as Allah showed you His essence. And therefore he also said: [from al-Khafif] 'Keep for me an eye, perhaps one day before my death I will see with it the one who saw You.' And it is also answered that the speech is about the divine presence, and the 'vision' is interpreted as heart-vision, about which he said: [from al-Tawil] 'Grant us, with the beloved, Your vision to which the hearts of the saints hasten.' So his saying 'He permitted my eye' means my heart, and he called it 'eye' metaphorically, because the speech is in the mode of allusion, since it is not explicit about the Supreme Essence.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage contains an objection and its answer. The objector cites the poetry of Ibn al-Farid, which seems to claim that he saw Allah physically in this world. The objector argues that if someone claims such, he becomes a disbeliever according to one opinion. The author provides two answers. The first answer interprets the poetry as addressing the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), not Allah directly. The phrase 'He favored my hearing with 'lan'' refers to the Prophet's response 'lan tarani' (You will not see Me) from the story of Moses. The poet is asking the Prophet not to give him that answer. Similarly, 'And if I ask You' is addressed to the Prophet, asking him to show his essence as Allah showed it to him. The second answer interprets the vision as heart-vision (ru'ya qalbiyya), not physical sight. The poet's word 'eye' is metaphorical for the heart. The author emphasizes that the poetry is not explicit about the divine essence, but rather uses allusion (kinaaya).

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The poetry must be interpreted allegorically: either addressed to the Prophet or as heart-vision, not as literal physical sight.

?

The Prophet's Miracles and Perfect Character as Proof
Enumerates miracles and describes perfect character as proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet Muhammad's miracles and his perfect character together provide compelling evidence for his truthfulness and prophethood.

Core Idea
Miracles and flawless character form an unbreakable proof of prophethood.

This lesson explores how the author presents the Prophet's miracles and his impeccable character as two interlocking testimonies. The miracles show divine intervention; the character shows a human perfection that no enemy could gainsay. Together, they leave no room for honest doubt.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Notice how the author first lists specific miracles and then describes the Prophet's character.
2
Identify the two categories of evidence
The passage presents two main proofs: miraculous events (water from fingers, blessing in food) and personal qualities (good character, forbearance, knowledge, bravery).
3
Reflect on the significance of knowledge without learning
The author emphasizes that the Prophet acquired knowledge without formal education, born among an unlettered people. This is a subtle miracle in itself.
4
Consider the testimony of enemies
The passage concludes that even enemies could find no fault and testified to his perfection. Ask yourself: why is this a strong argument?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصابع، وظهور البركة في الأطعمة والأشربة(٢)، وغير ذلك مما لا يحصى كثرة . مع ما كان عليه من حُسْن الخُلُق، الذي لا يراه أحد إلا ويقطع أنه ليس بكذاب، وإن كان يقع من الضَّالين العناد. ومن كمال خلقه تمام الحلم والعلم مع كونه ولد في قوم لا يعرفون شيئاً، من غير أن يتعاطى أسباب العلم، ووفور البركة، أكله جداً، فيقدم حيث تحجم الأبطال، ويقف حيث يفر عند شدّة مع قلة الهول صناديد الرّجال، ويثبت على حاله من الدعوى لدى شدائد الأهوال، حتّى لم يجد أعداؤه إليه مطعناً في حال من الأحوال، بل شهد له العدوُّ والحبيب بوُفُور الكمال والإفضال.
The fingers, and the appearance of blessing in foods and drinks, and other things whose abundance cannot be counted. Along with what he had of good character, which no one sees except that he is certain that he is not a liar, even if stubbornness occurs from the misguided. And from the perfection of his character is complete forbearance and knowledge despite his being born among a people who knew nothing, without his acquiring the means of knowledge, and abundant blessing, his eating was great? He advances where the heroes hold back, and stands where the elite flee at the intensity of fear, and he remains firm in his claim during severe terrors, until his enemies could find no point of attack against him in any circumstance; rather, both the enemy and the friend testified to his abundant perfection and beneficence.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a descriptive argument for the truthfulness of Prophet Muhammad's prophethood by listing his miracles and his perfect character. It begins by citing two specific miracles: water flowing from his fingers and blessing appearing in food and drink (referencing hadith). Then it notes that these and many other miracles are too numerous to count. The text then shifts to his moral perfection: his good character is such that no fair-minded person can doubt his honesty, even though stubborn people may still deny him. It further describes his forbearance (hilm) and knowledge (ilm), emphasizing that he acquired these without formal education, being born among an illiterate people. Additionally, his abundant blessing (baraka) is mentioned, and his bravery: he leads where even the bravest hesitate, and stands firm when others flee. This steadfastness in his claim during the direst situations left his enemies with no ground to accuse him of falsehood. In summary, both enemies and friends acknowledged his complete perfection and excellence.

The Weighing of Deeds and the Prophet's Basin
The author explains the weighing of deeds and the belief in the Prophet's Basin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrines of the weighing of deeds (al-mizan) and the Prophet's Basin (al-hawd), including the evidence from the hadith of the card and the descriptions in the sahihs.

Core Idea
The scales measure deeds, and the Basin quenches the faithful; both are true.

This lesson presents two interconnected eschatological beliefs: the weighing of deeds to determine reward and punishment, and the Prophet's Basin from which the righteous will drink. The author provides scriptural evidence, including the famous hadith of the card, and clarifies important details such as that every prophet has a basin. The passage emphasizes the importance of believing in these matters without delving into unnecessary details about their sequence.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening on weighing scrolls and the hadith of the card
Start from 'وقيل : توزن الصُّحُف' up to the verse 'فَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ'. This introduces the concept of weighing the scrolls and points to the hadith of the card as evidence.
2
Examine the hadith of the card in detail
The passage includes a lengthy narration of the hadith of the card. Read it to see how a single card bearing the shahada outweighs mountains of sins.
3
Study the description of the Prophet's Basin
Read from 'الإيمان بالحوض' to the end of the passage. Note the vivid details from the sahihs: the size, the water, the cups.
4
Understand the author's clarifications
The author clarifies that every prophet has a basin and discusses the order between the Basin, Scales, and Path. Focus on the obligatory belief without insisting on precise sequence.
The final sentence is incomplete in the source, so we take the general point.

(۲) أخرجه الترمذي (٢٦۳۹) ، والحاكم في ((المستدرك ) (٦/١) عن عبد الله بن عمرو ها الإيمان بالحوض وفي الصحيحين : حوضي مسيرة شهر وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيض من اللبن، وريحه أطيب من المسك، وكيزانه أكثر من نجوم السماء من شرب منه لا يظمأ أبداً». والصحيح أنَّ لكلّ نبي حوضاً، فليس من خصوصيات نبينا ، وأنّه يكون قبل الميزان . يعذب بقدره، فإن لم يكن له إلا حسنات فقط أو سيئات فقط؛ وضعت الصَّنج في الكفَّة الأخرى . قوله : (وفي الصَّحيحين» . . . إلخ ) : وقد ورد فيما أوحى الله إلى عيسى في صفة نبينا : له حوض أبعد من مكة إلى مطلع الشَّمس، فيه آنية مثل نجوم السَّماء، وله كل لون شراب الجنَّة، وطعم كلّ ثمار الجنة (٢) . قوله : (والصَّحيح أنَّ لكلِّ نبي حوضاً (۳) : أي : ولم يصح أن حوض صالح ضرع ناقته (٤) . قوله : (وأنَّه يكون قبل الميزان أي وهل هو قبل الصراط أو بعده قولان؟ وبالجملة : فالواجب علينا اعتقاد أنه ثابت، وجَهْل تقدمه على
And it is said: the scrolls in which the deeds are written are weighed, based on the fact that good deeds are distinguished from bad deeds by a book, and the hadith of the card bears witness to this. And there are weights of atoms by which the amount of difference is known, to realize complete justice. So whoever does an atom's weight of good shall see it, and whoever does an atom's weight of evil shall see it. (1) Belief in the Basin. (The Basin) meaning: the Basin of the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, and many hadiths about it have been narrated reaching the level of tawatur. His statement: (The hadith of the card) meaning: indeed there has been narrated what means: 'A servant had ninety-nine records of sins written against him, each record as far as the eye can see. They are placed in the pan of evil deeds. God says to him: O My servant, did you do a good deed? He says: No, my Lord. He says: But you have a trust with Us. Then he orders that a card be brought out, small as a fingertip, on which is written: There is no god but God, Muhammad is the Messenger of God. It is placed in the pan of good deeds, and the records of sins fly away, and nothing weighs heavy with the name of God. Then He says: Take My servant to Paradise by My favor and forgiveness.' (2) A leaf. His statement: (by which the amount of difference is known) meaning: the evil deeds are placed opposite the good deeds. If one outweighs the other, a weight is placed equal to the excess, and he is rewarded or punished accordingly. Or (1) Surah al-Zalzalah: (87). (2) Narrated by al-Tirmidhi (2639) and al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak (6/1) from Abdullah ibn Amr. Belief in the Basin. And in the Two Sahihs: 'My Basin is a month's journey, its corners are equal. Its water is whiter than milk, its smell is better than musk, and its cups are more numerous than the stars of the sky. Whoever drinks from it will never thirst.' And the correct view is that every prophet has a basin, so it is not exclusive to our Prophet, and that it is before the Scales. He is punished according to the excess. If he has only good deeds or only bad deeds, the weight is placed in the other pan. His statement: (And in the Two Sahihs ... etc.): And it has been narrated in what God revealed to Jesus regarding the description of our Prophet: 'He has a basin farther than Mecca to the rising of the sun. In it are vessels like the stars of the sky, and it contains every color of the wine of Paradise and the taste of every fruit of Paradise.' (2) His statement: (And the correct view that every prophet has a basin (3)) meaning: it is not established that the basin of Salih is the udder of his she-camel. (4) His statement: (And that it is before the Scales) meaning: is it before the Path or after? Two opinions. In summary: what is obligatory upon us is to believe that it is established, and ignorance of its precedence over
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage addresses two interconnected eschatological doctrines: the weighing of deeds (al-mizan) and the Prophet's Basin (al-hawd). The author begins by discussing the weighing of the scrolls. He states that some scholars hold that the scrolls containing the deeds are weighed, because good and bad deeds are distinguished in a book. To support this, he cites the hadith of the card (hadith al-bitaqa), which is presented in detail: a man who had ninety-nine records of sins is saved by a small card bearing the shahada, which outweighs all the sins. The author then explains that there are weights (sanaj) the size of atoms to measure the exact difference between good and evil deeds, ensuring complete justice, and he quotes the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Zalzalah. Next, he introduces the belief in the Basin (al-hawd), describing it as the Basin of the Messenger of God, supported by numerous mutawatir hadiths. He then gives a detailed description from the Two Sahihs (Bukhari and Muslim): the Basin is a month's journey wide, its water is white, its smell is fragrant, and its cups are countless; whoever drinks from it never thirsts again. The author then clarifies that the correct position is that every prophet has a basin, so it is not a unique feature of our Prophet Muhammad. Furthermore, the Basin occurs before the Scales (al-mizan). The author continues the discussion of the Scales, explaining that if someone has only good or only bad deeds, the weight is placed in the opposite pan. He then adds more transmitted evidence: in what God revealed to Jesus, the Prophet's Basin is described as huge, with vessels like stars and all the delights of Paradise. He also refutes a weak tradition that the basin of Prophet Salih was the udder of his she-camel. Finally, he discusses whether the Basin is before the Sirat (the Path) or after, noting two opinions, but emphasizes that the obligatory belief is simply that it is established, not necessarily knowing its precise order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only Prophet Muhammad has a basin.
Correction: The author states that the correct view is that every prophet has a basin, so it is not exclusive.

Checkpoint
What is the correct position regarding the Prophet's Basin relative to other prophets?
A) Only Prophet Muhammad has a basin.
B) Every prophet has a basin.
C) Only a few prophets have basins.
D) The basin is only for the righteous believers.

Key Takeaway
The weighing of deeds is just, and the Prophet's Basin is a gift for all prophets, but our Prophet's basin is particularly described in great detail.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadith of the card shows that a single statement of faith can outweigh a lifetime of sins. What is the state of your own shahada—is it the weightiest reality in your life, or have you reduced it to a mere phrase? Today, commit to reviving its meaning in your heart and actions.
?
The Basin is a gift from the Prophet to his followers, yet many ignore it. Do you truly long to drink from it, or are you distracted by the fleeting pleasures of this world? What will you change in your daily life to ensure you are among those who will be granted that drink?
?
The scales measure deeds down to the atom. How does that knowledge change the way you view a small act of kindness or a minor sin? Will you still neglect the 'small' sins or dismiss the 'small' good deeds, knowing they will appear on the scale?

Divine Transcendence
beginner
5 min
The Life and Status of Martyrs
Al-Sawi explains the life of martyrs and the reason for their name.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief that martyrs (shuhada') are alive in their graves and receive sustenance from Allah, the basis for their name, and the conditions for earning the full reward.

Core Idea
Martyrs are alive with Allah, enjoying Paradise, even while their bodies are in the grave.

The Qur'an and prophetic traditions affirm that those killed in the path of Allah are not dead but alive. Al-Sawi clarifies this special life, explains why martyrs are called 'witnesses', and distinguishes between those who fight for Allah's word and those who fight for worldly gain. This passage lays the foundation for understanding a key belief of the unseen world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the English translation. Let the author's own words come through before interpreting.
Notice the Quranic verse is quoted in the middle.
2
Identify the Quranic proof
Locate the verse from Surah Al-Imran (169) and note how it serves as the primary evidence for the life of martyrs.
The verse says they are 'alive with their Lord, provided for'.
3
Examine the two reasons for the name
Find the two explanations for why martyrs are called 'shuhada''. Understand each one: (a) their souls entered Paradise early, (b) Allah and angels testified for them.
These are not mutually exclusive but complementary.
4
Note the conditions and exception
Notice that the ruling of martyrdom extends to those killed in other just causes, but excludes those who fought for worldly motives like booty or bravery.
Sincerity (ikhlas) is essential for full reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشهداء أحياء في قبورهم قتلوا في جهاد الكفَّار لإعلاء كلمة الله وكحياة الشُّهداء، وهم من تعالى، حتى إنهم يأكلون ويشربون ويتنعمون في الجنَّة قال تعالى (وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ الَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَتَّاً بَلْ أَحْيَاءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ ) وإن لم تُعلّم كيفية هذه الحياة، إذ هي غير معقولة لأكثر البشر. وسُمُّوا شهداء لأنَّ أرواحهم شَهِدت دارَ السَّلام؛ أي: حضرتها ودخلتها، بخلاف غيرهم فإنَّه لا يدخلها إلا يوم القيامة، أو لأنّ الله وملائكته شهدوا له بالموافاة. وقوله : (في جهاد الكفَّار مثله من قتل على الحقِّ؛ كقتال البغاة، وقطَّاع الطريق، وإقامة الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر. وقوله : (الإعلاء كلمة الله : أخرج به من قاتل لا لإعلاء كلمة الله، بل للغنيمة، أو لإظهار الشَّجاعة ؛ فإنَّ له حكم شهداء الدُّنيا من عدم غسلهم والصَّلاة عليهم لا ثوابهم الكامل.
The martyrs are alive in their graves; they are killed in jihad against the disbelievers for the elevation of the word of Allah. And like the life of the martyrs, they are from those exalted, such that they eat, drink, and enjoy in Paradise. Allah said: 'Do not think that those who are killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather, they are alive with their Lord, provided for.' Even if the manner of this life is not known, for it is incomprehensible to most humans. They are called 'shuhada'' (witnesses) because their souls witnessed the abode of peace, i.e., they attended and entered it, unlike others who will not enter it until the Day of Resurrection; or because Allah and His angels witnessed for them with a good end. And his saying: 'in jihad against the disbelievers, similarly for one killed on behalf of the truth, such as fighting rebels, highway robbers, and establishing commanding good and forbidding evil.' And his saying: 'for the elevation of the word of Allah' excludes one who fought not for the elevation of the word of Allah, but for booty or to show bravery; such a one has the worldly ruling of the martyrs (not washed, prayers not offered over him) but not their complete reward.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the life and status of martyrs (shuhada'). It begins by affirming that martyrs are alive in their graves, specifically those killed in jihad for the sake of exalting Allah's word. It then likens them to the living, noting they eat, drink, and enjoy the blessings of Paradise, citing the Quranic verse from Surah Al-Imran (169). The author acknowledges that the manner of this life is not fully known and is beyond human comprehension. Then, he explains the reason for their name 'shuhada' (witnesses): either because their souls have already witnessed and entered Paradise (Dar al-Salam), unlike ordinary believers who will enter only on Judgment Day, or because Allah and His angels have witnessed that they died in a state of faith. Next, he clarifies two points: first, that the ruling of a martyr also applies to anyone killed in a just cause (like fighting rebels or bandits, or enjoining good and forbidding evil). Second, he specifies that 'for the elevation of Allah's word' excludes those who fight for worldly motives like booty or show of bravery; such individuals receive only the worldly rulings of a martyr (i.e., their bodies are not washed nor funeral prayer performed) but do not attain the full spiritual reward.

Key Terms
شهداء
حياة البرزخ
جهاد
إعلاء كلمة الله
الشهداء الدنيويون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The life of martyrs is a physical life like the worldly life; they can interact with the living.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that this life is special, unknown in its manner, and incomprehensible to most humans; it is a spiritual life in the grave with rewards in Paradise.

Checkpoint
Why are martyrs called 'shuhada' according to the passage?
A) Because they testify against the disbelievers on Judgment Day
B) Because their souls have already entered Paradise, or because Allah and His angels witnessed their good end
C) Because they saw the angels at death
D) Because they are alive in the grave and can speak to visitors

Key Takeaway
Martyrs (shuhada') live a special life in the grave, receiving provision from Allah, and are called shuhada' because their souls entered Paradise or because Allah and His angels witnessed for them; full reward depends on sincere intention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you engage in any struggle—whether in preaching, teaching, or personal growth—do you honestly examine whether your motive is truly to elevate Allah's word, or are you driven by pride, recognition, or personal gain? How does this lesson force you to recalibrate your intentions today?
?
If you were to die at this moment, would you have the confidence that your soul has already 'witnessed Paradise' through sincere faith and action, or would you be uncertain? What concrete step can you take right now to earn that witness?
